Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Word Accepted in Matters Only She Knows
Explains acceptance of wife's testimony in exclusive knowledge matters with conditional divorce examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting the wife's word in matters only she can know and apply it to conditional divorce scenarios.

Core Idea
In matters only she can know, the wife's word is accepted as proof — her testimony is sufficient without additional evidence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key principle in Hanafi family law: when a matter is known only to the wife, such as menstruation or love, her statement is taken as true. The author cites agreement of the four imams and extends the logic to conditional divorce. However, a nuanced dispute arises when the husband and wife disagree on the condition itself, and in that specific case the husband's word is taken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Understand that the wife's word is authoritative in matters only she can know, such as her own menstruation or love.
This is the core principle being established.
2
Recognize the proof
Note the proof: agreement of the four Imams (ijma) and her trustworthiness as she is commanded to disclose what is in her womb.
Ijma is a strong proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply to conditional divorce
Apply the principle: if the husband's conditional divorce (ta'liq) depends on a matter only she knows, then her statement triggers the divorce.
Example: 'If you menstruate, you are divorced.'
4
Distinguish the disputed case
Contrast with the scenario where the condition refers to something external (e.g., 'if you are without sin'). Here the husband's word is taken because he is claiming a restriction that she denies.
This highlights the limits of the principle.
5
Understand the analogy
The acceptance of the wife's word in exclusive matters is analogized to her word being accepted in 'iddah and prohibition of intercourse.
This shows consistency across fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وما لا يعلم إلا منها فالقول لها في حقها كأن حضت فأنت طالق وفلانة أو إن كنت تحبيني فأنت طالق وفلانة فقالت حضت أو أحبك طلقت فقط عليه الأئمة الأربعة هي لأنها أمينة مأمورة بإظهار ما في رحمها وفائدته ترتيب أحكام الطهر وهو فرع قبول قولها كما قبل إخبارها بالحيض في انقضاء العدة وحرمة جماعها وبالطهر وبقولها طهرت في اليمين تأمل جداً اهـ ما رأيته أقول: وهذا هو الذي يظهر لأنهما اتفقا على أصل الحلف واختلفا في القيد وهو من غير ذنب والزوج يدعي وجود القيد وهي تنكره فكأنه يدعي بذلك عدم وقوع الطلاق وهي تدعي وقوعه فالقول له ويؤيده ما سيأتي عند قول المصنف ولا في أنت طالق إن شاء الله حيث قال : ويشمل ما إذا ادعى الاستثناء وأنكرته فإن القول قوله وكذا في دعوى الشرط قوله : (وبالطهر وبقولها طهرت في حله كذا فيما رأيناه من النسخ والظاهر أن الواو في قوله «وبقولها» زائدة من قلم الناسخ لأن المعنى وكما قبل إخبارها بالطهر بقولها طهرت في حل الجماع قوله :
His saying: (And what is not known except from her, then the statement is hers in her right) like 'If you menstruate, you are divorced,' and 'So-and-so,' or 'If you love me, you are divorced,' and 'So-and-so.' So if she says 'I menstruated' or 'I love you,' she is divorced only. The four Imams agreed on her because she is trustworthy, commanded to disclose what is in her womb, and its benefit is the arrangement of rulings of purity, which is a branch of accepting her statement, just as her report of menstruation is accepted in the completion of the waiting period and the prohibition of intercourse, and by purity and by her saying 'I am pure' in an oath. Reflect deeply... I say: This is what appears, because they agreed on the basis of the oath and differed on the restriction, which is 'without sin,' and the husband claims the restriction exists and she denies it, so it is as if he thereby claims the non-occurrence of divorce, and she claims its occurrence, so the statement is his. This is supported by what will come in the words of the author: 'Nor in 'You are divorced if Allah wills' where he said: And it includes when he claims an exception and she denies it, then the statement is his, and likewise in the claim of a condition.' His saying: (And by purity and by her saying 'I am pure' in its permissibility) is as we have seen in the copies, and it appears that the 'waw' in his statement 'and by her saying' is extra from the pen of the copyist, because the meaning is: just as her report of purity by her saying 'I am pure' is accepted in the permissibility of intercourse.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that in matters which only the wife can know, her statement is accepted without requiring her to prove it. Examples include menstruation and love (in the context of a conditional divorce). The author notes that all four Imams agree on this because she is trustworthy and commanded to disclose what is in her womb. The acceptance of her word in such matters is analogous to her word being accepted in matters of iddah and prohibition of intercourse. The author also discusses a case of dispute regarding a conditional oath where the husband and wife disagree on the condition, and concludes that the husband's word is taken in that specific case. The passage ends with a note about the word 'wa' in the text being redundant.

Key Terms
وما لا يعلم إلا منها (wa ma la yu'lam illa minha): Matters that are not known except from the wife, such as menstruation, love, etc.
الحيض (al-hayd): Menstruation; a matter only the woman can know.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In conditional divorce, if the condition is 'If you menstruate, you are divorced,' and she says she menstruated, what happens?
A) She is not divorced
B) She is divorced
C) She must bring two witnesses
D) The husband's word is taken

Key Takeaway
The wife's word is accepted without proof in matters only she can know, due to her trustworthiness and the necessity of the situation.

Talaq — Divorce

Wife's Statement in Conditional Divorce: Accepted Only for Herself
Commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq expanding the ruling that the wife's statement about a condition known only to her is accepted only regarding herself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding a wife's claim about a condition known only to her in a suspended divorce, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on her being trustworthy (amīnah) in her own affairs but accused (muttahamah) in the rights of others.

Core Idea
The wife's word on conditions only she knows is accepted for herself, not for her co-wives.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband suspends divorce on a condition that only the wife can verify—such as her menstruation or her love for him—her statement is given legal weight. However, this acceptance is limited to her own case. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this distinction and its application when multiple wives are involved, as explained by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq in its commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the wife's claim that a condition (known only to her) in a suspended divorce has occurred. The ruling: her statement is accepted (tusaddaq) and divorce takes effect for her alone.
The act is her statement, not the divorce itself.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The commentator states that the wife is deemed trustworthy (amīnah) and commanded to disclose what is in her womb. This is derived from the Shariah's acceptance of her word in matters of menstruation and purity, which are foundational for rulings on iddah and marital intercourse.
The proof is not a direct text but a qiyas based on established principles.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illah) is that the wife alone has access to the knowledge; necessity (darurah) requires accepting her word. She is muttahamah (accused) only regarding others' rights, hence her statement does not bind them.
The analogy to an heir's acknowledgment of a debt clarifies the limitation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text says 'upon the four Imams' indicating broad agreement. However, there is an intra-Hanafi nuance: the author of Fath al-Qadir considers Imam Muhammad's formulation 'awjah' (more correct).
No cross-madhhab dispute is presented.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that her statement is accepted for herself only. This is consistent across the Hanafi school, as emphasized by the commentator.
The tarjih is implicit in the commentator's presentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب التعليق برهنت وما لا يعلم إلا منها فالقول لها في حقها كأن حضت فأنت طالق وفلانة أو أن كنت تحبيني فأنت طالق وفلانة فقالت حضت أو أحبك طلقت فقط وبرؤية الدم لا هي وقد نقله عن لا إثبات التضحية لأنها لا مطالب بها فصار كما إذا شهدوا أنه لم يحج. غاية الأمر أن هذا النفي مما يحيط به علم الشاهد ولكنه لا يميز بين نفي ونفي تيسيراً .اهـ. فمشكل ولذا قال في فتح القدير: إن قول محمد أوجه ظاهره تسليم أنها على الشرط مقبولة ولو نفياً المبسوط أيضاً وسيأتي تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى ولو قال المصنف ولو ادعى عليه أن الشرط قد وجد وأنكر فالقول له إلا إذا شهدت البينة لكان أولى لأنه لا يشترط دعوى المرأة للطلاق ولا أن تبرهن لأن الشهادة على عتق الأمة وطلاق المرأة تقبل حسبة بلا دعوى، ولا يشترط حضور المرأة والأمة لكن يشترط حضور الزوج والمولى صح تحضر المرأة ليشير إليها الشهود ط. لو شهد أنه أبان امرأته فلانة فقالت لم يطلقني وقال الزوج ليس اسمها فلانة وشهدا أن اسمها فلانة فالقاضي يفرق بينهما ويماثله عتق الأمة، فلو شهدا أنه حررها وأن اسمها كذا وقالت لم يحررني فالقاضي يحكم بعتقها والشهادة بحرمة المصاهرة والإيلاء والظهار بدون الدعوى تقبل ويشترط حضور المشهود عليه وقيل لا تقبل بدون الدعوى في الإيلاء والظهار وفي عتق الأمة والطلاق بدون الدعوى قيل يحلف وقيل لا فليتأمل عند الفتوى، كذا جامع الفصولين. وفي القنية : ادعت أنه طلقها من غير شرط والزوج يقول طلقتها بالشرط ولم يوجد فالبينة فيه بينة المرأة، ولو ادعت عليه أنه حلف لا يضربها وادعى هو أنه لا يضربها من غير ذنب وأقاما البينة فيثبت كلا الأمرين وتطلق بأيهما كان .اهـ. وفي القنية من باب البينتين المتضادتين : ولو قال لامرأته إن شربت مسكراً بغير إذنك فأمرك بيدك فأقامت بينة على وجود الشرط وأقام الزوج بينة أنه كان بإذنها فبينة المرأة أولى اهـ. حله في وهي

قوله: (وما لا يعلم إلا منها فالقول لها في حقها) أي كأن حضت فأنت طالق وفلانة أو إن كنت تحبيني فأنت طالق وفلانة فقالت حضت أو أحبك طلقت فقط عليه الأئمة الأربعة هي لأنها أمينة مأمورة بإظهار ما في رحمها وفائدته ترتيب أحكام الطهر وهو فرع قبول قولها كما قبل إخبارها بالحيض في انقضاء العدة وحرمة جماعها وبالطهر وبقولها طهرت في [؟] حله كذا فيما رأيناه من النسخ والظاهر أن الواو في قوله «وبقولها» زائدة من قلم الناسخ لأن المعنى وكما قبل إخبارها بالطهر بقولها طهرت في حل الجماع قوله : متهمة في حق غيرها إن كذبها الزوج وإن صدقها طلقت فلانة أيضاً. والحاصل أن المنظور إليه في حقها شرعاً الإخبار به لأنها أمينة وفي حق ضرتها متهمة وشهادتها على ذلك شهادة فرد ولا بعد في أن يقبل قول الإنسان في حق نفسه لا في حق غيره كأحد الورثة إذا أقر بدين على الميت اقتصر على نصيبه إذا لم يصدقه الباقون والمشتري إذا أقر بالمبيع لمستحق لا يرجع بالثمن على البائع كذا في فتح القدير. وقد يقال : إن المقر في المسألتين لم يتعد ضرر إقراره إلى أحد وهنا تعدى إلى الزوج بقطع العصمة مع كونها متهمة في حق نفسها أيضاً ولا بد من قيام الحيض عند الإخبار، أما بعد الانقطاع فلا لأنه ضرورة فيشترط قيام الشرط بخلاف إن حضت حيضة حيث يقبل قولها في الطهر الذي يلي الحيضة لا قبله ولا بعده لأنها أخبرت عن الشرط حال عدمه والمعنى فيه أن الشرع جعلها أمينة فيما تخبر به عن الحيض والطهر ضرورة إقامة الأحكام المتعلقة بهما فما دامت الأحكام قائمة كان الاسمان قائمين من جهة الشرع فتصدق، وإذا كانت الأحكام منقضية كان الاسمان غير ثابتين فلا تصدق بخلاف المودع لو قال رددتها أو هلكت يصدق ولا يشترط لتصديقه قيام الأمانة لأنه صار أميناً من جهة صاحب المال صريحاً وابتداء لا لضرورة حيث ائتمنه صاحب المال مطلقاً؛ كذا في المعراج قيد بقوله إن حضت لأنه لو قال لامرأتيه إن حضتما فأنتما طالقان فقالتا حضنا تطلق واحدة منهما إلا أن يصدقهما، فإن صدق إحداهما وكذب الأخرى طلقت المكذبة. وإن كن ثلاثاً فقال ذلك فقلن حضنا لم تطلق واحدة منهن إلا أن يصدقهن، وكذا إن صدق إحداهن، فإن صدق ثنتين فقط طلقت المكذبة دون المصدقات ولو كن أربعاً والمسألة بحالها لم يطلقن إلا أن يصدقهن، وكذا إن صدق إحداهن أو اثنتين وإن صدق ثلاثاً فقط طلقت المكذبة دون المصدقات والوجه ظاهر من الشرح وفي المحيط قال لنسائه الأربع إذا حضتن حيضة فأنتن طوالق فقالت واحدة حضت حيضة وصدقها الزوج طلقن لأن شرط وقوع الطلاق عليهن حيضة واحدة منهن لأن اجتماعهن على حيضة واحدة لا يتصور فيجعل ذلك مجازاً عن حيضة إحداهن كما لو قال لامرأتيه إذا حضتما حيضة فأنتما طالقان فحاضت إحداهما طلقتا وإن كذبها طلقت وحدها تطليقة لأنها مصدقة في حقها دون ضراتها، ولو هي لا والوجه ظاهر من الشرح قال فيه : والأصل فيه أن حيض جميعهن شرط لوقوع الطلاق عليهن ولم تطلق واحدة منهن حتى ترى جميعهن الحيض، وإن حاضت بعضهن يكون ذلك بعض العلة يثبت بها الحكم. فإن قلن جميعاً قد حضنا لا يثبت حيض كل واحدة منهن إلا في حقها ولا يثبت في حق غيرها إلا أن يصدقهن فيثبت في حق الجميع، وإن صدق البعض وكذب البعض ينظر، فإن كانت المكذبة واحدة طلقت هي وحدها تمام الشرط في حقها لأن قولها مقبول في حق نفسها وقد صدق غيرها فتم الشرط فيها، ولا يطلق غيرها لأن المكذبة لا يقبل قولها في حق غيرها فلم يتم
The Book of Divorce, Chapter of Conditional Suspension. She proved [?] and that which is not known except from her, so the statement is hers regarding herself, such as if he said: 'If you menstruate, then you are divorced and so-and-so,' or 'If you love me, then you are divorced and so-and-so,' and she said 'I menstruated' or 'I love you,' then she alone is divorced. And by seeing blood, she is not [divorced]... And he narrated from... etc. His statement: '(And that which is not known except from her, so the statement is hers regarding herself)' means such as if he said: 'If you menstruate, then you are divorced and so-and-so,' or 'If you love me, then you are divorced and so-and-so,' and she said 'I menstruated' or 'I love you,' then she alone is divorced, according to the four Imams, because she is trustworthy, commanded to disclose what is in her womb... and the summary is that the consideration in her regard legally is the report because she is trustworthy, and in the regard of her co-wife she is accused, and her testimony is a single testimony...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that for matters known only to the wife, her statement is accepted only regarding herself. The commentary opens by reaffirming the ruling: if a husband makes divorce conditional on something only the wife knows, like her menstruation or love for him, and she claims the condition occurred, she is divorced alone—not her co-wives. The basis (ta'lil) is that the wife is aminah (trustworthy) in matters of her own body, as she is commanded to disclose what is in her womb. The author then contrasts this with her being accused (mutamah) regarding others. He draws an analogy: just as an heir's acknowledgment of a debt on the deceased only affects his own share, or a buyer's acknowledgment that the sold item belongs to another does not let him recover the price from the seller, similarly the wife's statement only affects herself. The commentary then discusses a potential objection: in the analogies, no harm extends to others, but here harm extends to the husband by severing the marital bond, yet the ruling remains because she is trusted in her own right. The author further explains that her statement is only accepted if the condition is still ongoing at the time of her report; after its cessation, the ruling does not apply, unlike a depository (muda') who is believed even after the period of trust. The passage then goes into detailed sub-rulings for multiple wives: if a husband addresses two, three, or four wives with a conditional divorce based on their menstruation, and they claim menstruation, the rulings vary based on the husband's confirmation or denial. The key principle remains: each wife's statement is accepted only for herself unless the husband confirms others. The original text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq is expanded with extensive explanation of the wisdom (hikmah) and legal reasoning.

Key Terms
أمينة (amīnah): The wife is considered trustworthy (trusted) in reporting matters related to her own body, such as menstruation or purity.
متهمة (muttahamah): The wife is considered accused (not trustworthy) when her statement affects the rights of others, such as her co-wives or the husband beyond herself.
تعليق (ta‘līq): Suspending the occurrence of divorce on a future condition (shart).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his two wives, 'If both of you menstruate, you are both divorced,' and each wife claims she menstruated, but the husband denies it, what happens?
A) Both wives are divorced.
B) Neither wife is divorced.
C) One wife is divorced according to her own claim.
D) The husband's denial is accepted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the wife's statement about a condition only she knows in a suspended divorce is accepted only for herself, not for her co-wives or the husband's rights beyond herself.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Suspension of Divorce on a Single Menstruation with Multiple Wives
Ruling with proof using qiyas khafi and multi-case scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a wife's report of menstruation is accepted only in her own case and distinguish scenarios where the husband's acknowledgment affects the divorce of co-wives.

Core Idea
A wife's word about her own menstruation is trusted by necessity, but it does not bind her co-wives.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a specific scenario in suspended divorce: when a husband conditions divorce on a single menstruation affecting multiple wives. The key ruling is that each wife is believed regarding her own menstruation out of legal necessity, but her report does not extend to her co-wives unless the husband acknowledges it. This leads to complex multi-wife scenarios which we will work through step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recognize that each wife is amīnah (trustworthy) concerning her own menstruation due to necessity, but she is accused regarding her co-wives. Her statement is accepted only in her own case.
This principle is derived from the necessity of establishing rulings related to menstruation.
2
Understand the qiyas to the depositary
The analogy with a depositary who claims return or loss of a deposit shows that trustworthiness can be limited. The depositary is entrusted explicitly; the wife is entrusted by the Lawgiver out of necessity, which limits the scope of her trustworthiness.
The illa is trustworthiness (amānah) but with the restriction of necessity.
3
Apply the timing condition
The wife's report is only accepted if menstruation is present at the time of her statement. If she reports after it ceases, her word is not accepted because the necessity no longer applies.
This contrasts with the depositary, whose trustworthiness continues regardless.
4
Work through the two-wife scenario
If the husband says to both wives 'If you menstruate, you are divorced' and both claim menstruation, but he denies both, only one divorce occurs because each is believed for herself, and the condition 'both menstruating' is not established for either in relation to the other.
If he acknowledges one, the acknowledged one's statement completes the condition for the other? Actually the text says only the denied one is divorced if he acknowledges one and denies the other.
5
Scale to three or four wives
For three or four wives, the same principles apply. If the husband denies all, only one divorce occurs. If he acknowledges some, the denied ones may be divorced only if they are the sole denier; if he denies more than one, none are divorced because their statements cannot support each other.
The reasoning is that the condition of all menstruating is not met for any wife due to lack of mutual corroboration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب التعليق
متهمة في حق غيرها إن كذبها الزوج وإن صدقها طلقت فلانة أيضاً. والحاصل أن المنظور إليه في حقها شرعاً الإخبار به لأنها أمينة وفي حق ضرتها متهمة وشهادتها على ذلك شهادة فرد ولا بعد في أن يقبل قول الإنسان في حق نفسه لا في حق غيره كأحد الورثة إذا أقر بدين على الميت اقتصر على نصيبه إذا لم يصدقه الباقون والمشتري إذا أقر بالمبيع لمستحق لا يرجع بالثمن على البائع كذا في فتح القدير. وقد يقال : إن المقر في المسألتين لم يتعد ضرر إقراره إلى أحد وهنا تعدى إلى الزوج بقطع العصمة مع كونها متهمة في حق نفسها أيضاً ولا بد من قيام الحيض عند الإخبار، أما بعد الانقطاع فلا لأنه ضرورة فيشترط قيام الشرط بخلاف إن حضت حيضة حيث يقبل قولها في الطهر الذي يلي الحيضة لا قبله ولا بعده لأنها أخبرت عن الشرط حال عدمه والمعنى فيه أن الشرع جعلها أمينة فيما تخبر به عن الحيض والطهر ضرورة إقامة الأحكام المتعلقة بهما فما دامت الأحكام قائمة كان الاسمان قائمين من جهة الشرع فتصدق، وإذا كانت الأحكام منقضية كان الاسمان غير ثابتين فلا تصدق بخلاف المودع لو قال رددتها أو هلكت يصدق ولا يشترط لتصديقه قيام الأمانة لأنه صار أميناً من جهة صاحب المال صريحاً وابتداء لا لضرورة حيث ائتمنه صاحب المال مطلقاً؛ كذا في المعراج قيد بقوله إن حضت لأنه لو قال لامرأتيه إن حضتما فأنتما طالقان فقالتا حضنا تطلق واحدة منهما إلا أن يصدقهما، فإن صدق إحداهما وكذب الأخرى طلقت المكذبة. وإن كن ثلاثاً فقال ذلك فقلن حضنا لم تطلق واحدة منهن إلا أن يصدقهن، وكذا إن صدق إحداهن، فإن صدق ثنتين فقط طلقت المكذبة دون المصدقات ولو كن أربعاً والمسألة بحالها لم يطلقن إلا أن يصدقهن، وكذا إن صدق إحداهن أو اثنتين وإن صدق ثلاثاً فقط طلقت المكذبة دون المصدقات والوجه ظاهر من الشرح وفي المحيط قال لنسائه الأربع إذا حضتن حيضة فأنتن طوالق فقالت واحدة حضت حيضة وصدقها الزوج طلقن لأن شرط وقوع الطلاق عليهن حيضة واحدة منهن لأن اجتماعهن على حيضة واحدة لا يتصور فيجعل ذلك مجازاً عن حيضة إحداهن كما لو قال لامرأتيه إذا حضتما حيضة فأنتما طالقان فحاضت إحداهما طلقتا وإن كذبها طلقت وحدها تطليقة لأنها مصدقة في حقها دون ضراتها، والوجه ظاهر من الشرح قال فيه : والأصل فيه أن حيض جميعهن شرط لوقوع الطلاق عليهن ولم تطلق واحدة منهن حتى ترى جميعهن الحيض، وإن حاضت بعضهن يكون ذلك بعض العلة يثبت بها الحكم. فإن قلن جميعاً قد حضنا لا يثبت حيض كل واحدة منهن إلا في حقها ولا يثبت في حق غيرها إلا أن يصدقهن فيثبت في حق الجميع، وإن صدق البعض وكذب البعض ينظر، فإن كانت المكذبة واحدة طلقت هي وحدها تمام الشرط في حقها لأن قولها مقبول في حق نفسها وقد صدق غيرها فتم الشرط فيها، ولا يطلق غيرها لأن المكذبة لا يقبل قولها في حق غيرها فلم يتم
قالت كل واحدة حضت حيضة طلقت كل واحدة تطليقة صدقها الزوج أو كذبها لأن كل واحدة مصدقة شرعاً فيما بينها وبين زوجها.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Suspension. She is accused in the right of others if the husband denies her, and if he acknowledges her, so-and-so is also divorced. The summary is that legally, what is considered is her report because she is trustworthy, but regarding her co-wife she is accused, and her testimony is like a single testimony. It is not far-fetched that one's statement is accepted in one's own case but not in the case of others, like one of the heirs if he admits a debt against the deceased, it is limited to his share if the others do not confirm him, and the buyer if he admits the sold item belongs to a claimant, he cannot recover the price from the seller, as in Fath al-Qadir. It may be said that the admitter in the two cases does not extend harm to anyone, but here harm extends to the husband by severing marital bond while she is also accused in her own case... it is necessary that menstruation be present at the time of reporting; after it ceases, it is not accepted because it is a necessity, so the condition must be present, unlike if she says 'I menstruated a menstruation' where her word is accepted about the purity period following the menstruation, not before or after, because she reports about a condition when it is absent. The meaning is that the Lawgiver made her trustworthy concerning her reports about menstruation and purity out of necessity for establishing rulings related to them. As long as the rulings are in effect, the two terms are established from a legal perspective, so she is believed; when the rulings cease, the terms are not established, so she is not believed, unlike the depositary if he says 'I returned it' or 'it was destroyed', he is believed and his trustworthiness does not require that he still be in possession, because he became a trustee by explicit agreement of the owner from the start, not out of necessity, since the owner entrusted him absolutely, as in al-Mi'raj. He restricted by saying 'if I menstruated' because if he said to his two wives 'if you both menstruate, you are both divorced' and they said 'we menstruated', only one of them is divorced unless he confirms them; if he confirms one and denies the other, the denied one is divorced. If there are three wives and he says that, then they say 'we menstruated', not one of them is divorced unless he confirms them; similarly, if he confirms one, and if he confirms only two, the denied one is divorced but not the confirmed ones. If there are four wives and the case is the same, they are not divorced unless he confirms them; similarly, if he confirms one or two, and if he confirms three only, the denied one is divorced but not the confirmed ones. The reasoning is clear from the commentary: the origin is that the menstruation of all of them is a condition for the occurrence of divorce on them, and not one of them is divorced until all of them have menstruated; if some menstruate, that is part of the cause and the ruling is established by it. If they all say 'we have menstruated', the menstruation of each one is not established except in her own case, and it is not established in the case of others unless he confirms them, then it is established for all. If he confirms some and denies others, then if the denied one is one, she alone is divorced because the condition is complete in her own case since her word is accepted in her own case and he has confirmed others, so the condition is complete for her; but the others are not divorced because the denied one's word is not accepted regarding others, so it is not complete. If he denies more than one, not one of them is divorced. The text: 'Each one said: I menstruated a menstruation, then each one is divorced one divorce, whether the husband confirms or denies her, because each one is legally truthful concerning herself and her husband.'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the suspension of divorce on a single menstruation with multiple wives. The author explains the principle: each wife is believed regarding her own menstruation (as she is trustworthy out of necessity), but not regarding her co-wives. The husband's acknowledgment affects the others. The text begins with a general rule: a wife is accused in the right of her co-wife, so her statement alone does not affect the co-wife. However, if the husband acknowledges, the co-wife is also divorced. The reasoning is likened to an heir admitting a debt or a buyer admitting ownership—accepted only in one's own case. The condition of menstruation must be present at the time of report; after it passes, the report is not accepted. The text then presents scenarios with two, three, and four wives. In each case, if all claim menstruation and the husband denies all, only one divorce occurs (since each is believed for herself, and the condition of all menstruating is not established for any). If he confirms some, the condition is completed for the confirmed ones via the confessed wife's statement, and the unconfirmed ones are divorced only if they are the sole denier. For four wives who each claim one menstruation (conditional on a single occurrence), each gets one divorce regardless of acknowledgment, because each is believed for herself and the condition is a single menstruation from any one of them.

Key Terms
أمينة (amīnah): Trustworthy; legally relied upon for reports about menstruation/purity
مصدقة (muṣaddaqah): One whose statement is believed or confirmed by the husband
مكذبة (mukadhdhabah): One whose statement is denied by the husband

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his two wives, 'If you both menstruate, you are divorced,' and they both claim menstruation, how many are divorced if he denies both?
A) Both are divorced
B) Only one is divorced
C) Neither is divorced
D) The one who reported first is divorced

Key Takeaway
A wife's report of menstruation is accepted only in her own case; the husband's acknowledgment extends the effect to co-wives, but the condition of menstruation must be present at the time of report.

Recurring Condition and Acknowledgment in Talaq
Explains the effect of a recurring (kullama) condition and acknowledgment on number of divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of divorces each wife receives when a husband sets a recurring condition (kullama) and acknowledges some wives' reports.

Core Idea
Husband's acknowledgment extends the condition to all wives, multiplying divorces for those not acknowledged.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband pronounces a conditional divorce using 'kullama' (whenever), each occurrence of the condition triggers divorces for all wives. If wives report that the condition is fulfilled, the husband's acknowledgment (tasdiq) affects how many conditions are established for each wife. This lesson walks through the scenario of four wives and varying acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
The husband said 'Whenever you menstruate a menstruation, you are all divorced.' The word 'kullama' makes the condition recurring.
2
Categorize the Reports
Each wife claims one menstruation. The husband may deny all, confirm one, two, or three.
3
Count Established Menstruations per Wife
Each wife's own report establishes one menstruation for herself. Confirmation of another wife establishes that wife's menstruation for all others.
This is the key principle: tasdiq extends the effect.
4
Calculate Divorces
The number of divorces per wife equals the number of menstruations established in her case. For example, if husband confirms one, that wife's menstruation is established for all others, so the denied get two (her own + confirmed one).
5
Verify with Extreme Cases
Check if all denied: each gets one. If all confirmed: each gets three (since each wife's menstruation is established for all others? Actually passage says if confirms three, each confirmed gets three, denied gets four. Wait: need to follow the text. If confirms three, the three confirmed each have their own and the other two confirmed's, so three each? Passage says each confirmed gets three, denied gets four. So careful.
The denied gets four because she has her own plus three from confirmees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال كلما حضتن حيضة فأنتن طوالق فقالت كل واحدة حضت حيضة، فإن كذبهن طلقت كل واحدة تطليقة لأنه ثبت حيضة كل واحدة في حق نفسها خاصة دون صواحبها فلم يوجد في حق كل واحدة إلا شرط طلاق واحدة، وإن صدق واحدة دون الثلاث طلقت كل واحدة من الثلاث ثنتين والمصدقة واحدة لأنه ثبت في حق المصدقة دون حيض صواحبها وثبت في حق كل واحدة من المكذبات حيضتان حيضها بإخبارها وحيضة المصدقة بالتصديق، وإن صدق منهن اثنتين طلقت كل مصدقة اثنتين لوجود حيضتين في حق كل واحدة حيضتها وحيضة صاحبتها المصدقة وكل مكذبة ثلاثاً لوجود ثلاث حيض في حقها حيضتها وحيضتي المصدقتين، وإن صدق ثلاثاً طلقت كل واحدة ثلاثاً لثبوت ثلاث حيض في حق المصدقات وأربع حيض في حق المكذبة
اه.
If he said 'Whenever you menstruate a menstruation, you are all divorced,' and each one said 'I menstruated a menstruation,' then if he denies them all, each one is divorced one divorce because each one's menstruation is established only in her own case, not regarding her companions, so in the case of each only one condition of divorce exists. If he confirms one but not the other three, each of the three (the denied) is divorced two, and the confirmed one is divorced one, because in the case of the confirmed one, her companions' menstruation is not established, but in the case of each of the denied, two menstruations are established: her own by her report and the menstruation of the confirmed one by the confirmation. If he confirms two, each confirmed one is divorced two (her own and the other confirmed's), and each denied one is divorced three (her own and the two confirmed's). If he confirms three, each of the three confirmed is divorced three, and the denied one is divorced four.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents a scenario with four wives where the husband says 'Whenever you menstruate a menstruation, you are all divorced' (kullama condition, meaning each menstruation triggers a divorce for all). When each wife claims one menstruation, the number of divorces depends on the husband's acknowledgment. If he denies all, each gets one divorce (only her own menstruation counts). If he confirms one, that one's menstruation is established in the case of all, so the denied ones get two divorces (her own plus the confirmed one), the confirmed gets one. If he confirms two, each confirmed gets two, each denied gets three. If he confirms three, the confirmed get three, the denied gets four. The underlying principle: each wife is believed for herself, and the effect of confirmation extends to others, multiplying the number of conditions fulfilled.

Key Terms
كلما (kullamā): Whenever; indicates a recurring condition
تصديق (taṣdīq): Husband's confirmation of a wife's report

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the kullama scenario with four wives, if the husband confirms two wives, how many divorces does each confirmed wife receive?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The husband's acknowledgment of one wife's report extends that condition to all wives, multiplying the number of divorces for those not acknowledged.

Testimony for Birth in Suspended Divorce: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-madhhab dispute on evidence for birth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the testimony required to prove birth in a suspended divorce, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For birth in suspended divorce, Abu Hanifa requires standard testimony; the disciples accept a midwife's word alone.

In Hanafi law, when a husband suspends his wife's divorce on her giving birth, proving the birth becomes crucial. But what testimony suffices? This lesson unpacks a key intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples. Understanding this disagreement reveals how the school balances strict evidence rules with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Set the Context
Recall that a suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) triggers upon occurrence of a condition, such as birth. Proving the condition is essential for the divorce to take effect.
2
Identify the Points of Agreement
Note that co-wife's menstruation knowledge and other events like entry and speech are unanimously decided – the wife's statement is accepted only if no external knowledge exists. For birth, however, there is disagreement.
3
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa requires standard shahada: two male witnesses or one male and two females. Birth is a physical event like any other, so normal proof rules apply.
4
State the Disciples' Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the sole testimony of the midwife (qabilah), because childbirth is typically witnessed only by women, and requiring two males would be impractical.
5
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, if only a midwife testifies, the divorce does not occur; under the disciples, it does. This affects the wife's marital status and her right to maintenance.
6
Evaluate the Tarjih
The source text does not give a tarjih, but later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Jawharah, al-Hidayah) often prefer the disciples' view due to necessity (darurah) and custom (urf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الوقوع على الضرة لم ينحصر في تصديقه وإنما يتوقف على تصديقه إذا لم يعلم وجود الحيض منها، أما إذا علم طلقت فلانة أيضاً؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وقيد بكونه لا يعلم إلا منها لأنه لو كان يعلم من غيرها توقف الوقوع على تصديقه أو البينة كالدخول والكلام اتفاقاً. واختلفوا فيما لو علق طلاقها بولادتها فقالا يقع الطلاق بشهادة القابلة. وقال الإمام الأعظم : لا بد من شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين كما في الجوهرة. ولا يشمل ما لو علقه على فعل بغير إذنها لما في البزازية : إن شربت مسكراً يغير إذنك فأمرك بيدك وشرب ثم اختلفا في الإذن فالقول له والبينة لها وفي الصيرقية إن ذهبت إلى بيت أبي بغير إذنك فأنت طالق فادعى إذنها وأنكسرت فالقول له لأنه ينكر وقوع الطلاق مع أن الإذن لا يستفاد إلا . ر منها ولكن يطلع عليه بالقول بخلاف الحيض والمحبة والبغض ومن قبيل الدخول والكلام ما لو علق بقوله إن كنت جائعة في بيتي قال قاضيخان إن لم تكن جائعة في غير الصوم لا يكون حانثاً. ومنه ما لو علقه بقوله إن لم أشبعك من الجماع قال القاضي : إن جامعها حتى...
Then know that the occurrence [of divorce] upon the co-wife is not limited to his confirmation; rather it depends on his confirmation if the existence of menstruation from her is not known. If it is known, so-and-so is also divorced; as in al-Jawharah. It is restricted by that it is not known except from her, because if it were known from other than her, the occurrence depends on his confirmation or evidence, like entry and speech, unanimously. They differed on if he suspended her divorce on her birth: the two said divorce occurs by the testimony of the midwife. Imam A'zam said: two male witnesses or one male and two females are necessary, as in al-Jawharah. And it does not include if he suspended it on an action without her permission, as in al-Bazzaziyyah: 'If you drink an intoxicant without my permission, your affair is in your hand,' and she drank, then they differed on permission; his word is taken and her evidence is required. And in al-Sayyariqiyyah: 'If you go to your father's house without my permission, you are divorced,' and she claimed permission and he denied, his word is taken because he denies the occurrence of divorce, while permission cannot be known except ... from her, but it is known by speech, unlike menstruation, love, and hate. And from the category of entry and speech is what if he suspended by saying 'If you are hungry in my house,' Qadikhan said: If she is not hungry apart from fasting, he is not an oath-breaker. And from it is what if he suspended by saying 'If I do not satisfy you through intercourse,' al-Qadi said: 'If he has intercourse with her until...'
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage covers several distinct rulings. First, a note on the co-wife's divorce: if the husband is ignorant of the co-wife's menstruation, her statement is accepted only for herself; but if the menstruation is known (e.g., seen by others), then the co-wife is also divorced. This is unanimous. Second, a dispute regarding birth: if divorce is suspended on the wife's giving birth, Abu Hanifa (Imam A'zam) requires two male witnesses or one male and two females to prove the birth. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept the testimony of a single midwife (qabilah), because childbirth is usually witnessed by women. Third, conditions involving permission: if the husband suspends divorce on an act done without his permission (e.g., drinking intoxicant or going to father's house), and they differ on whether permission was given, the husband's word is taken (he denies the condition) because he denies the occurrence of divorce. The wife must provide evidence. This differs from menstruation, where the wife is believed because it is a hidden matter. Fourth, conditions like hunger: if he says 'If you are hungry in my house,' and she is hungry (not due to fasting), he is not an oath-breaker according to Qadikhan. The passage ends with an incomplete discussion of intercourse satisfaction.

Key Terms
قابلة (qābilah): Midwife; a woman who assists in childbirth
إذن (idhn): Permission from the husband

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what testimony is required to prove birth in a suspended divorce?
A) Testimony of one midwife
B) Testimony of one male and two females
C) Testimony of two men or one man and two women
D) The wife's own statement

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, proving birth for a suspended divorce involves a key dispute: Abu Hanifa demands standard testimony, while the disciples accept a midwife's word, with the latter often preferred in practice.

Conditional Divorce Based on Menstruation Claims by Multiple Wives
Ruling on calculation of divorces when multiple wives claim menstruation in conditional divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of divorces when a man conditionally divorces multiple wives based on menstruation, accounting for the husband's belief or disbelief in each wife's claim.

Core Idea
Each wife's menstruation claim binds herself; the husband's belief adds her menstruation to the other wives' count.

In Hanafi law, a wife's claim of menstruation is legally credible for herself, but when a husband conditionally divorces multiple wives upon menstruation, his belief or disbelief multiplies the number of divorces. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq teaches us to compute divorces by counting the menstruations established per wife, which includes her own claim and any co-wife's claim that the husband believes. Let's work through the scenarios step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Each wife's claim of menstruation is credible (musaddaqa) in her own right, regardless of the husband's belief. This establishes one menstruation for her.
This principle is based on the Hanafi maxim that women are trusted regarding their own menstruation.
2
Determine the effect of the husband's belief
When the husband believes a wife, her menstruation becomes established not only for herself but also for every other wife. This adds to the count of other wives' menstruations.
Disbelief does not negate her own claim, but it prevents her claim from being counted for others.
3
Count menstruations per wife
For each wife, count: (1) her own claim (always 1), plus (2) the number of co‑wives whose claims the husband believes. That total is the number of menstruations established for that wife.
Example: if 4 wives, husband believes 2 co‑wives, each co‑wife has 1 (own) + 1 (other believed) = 2; the disbelieved wife has 1 (own) + 2 (both believed) = 3.
4
Apply the conditional divorce clause
The husband said 'Whenever you menstruate, you are divorced.' Each menstruation triggers one divorce. So the number of divorces for each wife equals the number of menstruations counted for her.
The divorce occurs correctly if all conditions are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالت كل واحدة حضت حيضة طلقت كل واحدة تطليقة صدقها الزوج أو كذبها لأن كل واحدة مصدقة شرعاً فيما بينها وبين زوجها. ولو قال كلما حضتن حيضة فأنتن طوالق فقالت كل واحدة حضت حيضة، فإن كذبهن طلقت كل واحدة تطليقة لأنه ثبت حيضة كل واحدة في حق نفسها خاصة دون صواحبها فلم يوجد في حق كل واحدة إلا شرط طلاق واحدة، وإن صدق واحدة دون الثلاث طلقت كل واحدة من الثلاث ثنتين والمصدقة واحدة لأنه ثبت في حق المصدقة دون حيض صواحبها وثبت في حق كل واحدة من المكذبات حيضتان حيضها بإخبارها وحيضة المصدقة بالتصديق، وإن صدق منهن اثنتين طلقت كل مصدقة اثنتين لوجود حيضتين في حق كل واحدة حيضتها وحيضة صاحبتها المصدقة وكل مكذبة ثلاثاً لوجود ثلاث حيض في حقها حيضتها وحيضتي المصدقتين، وإن صدق ثلاثاً طلقت كل واحدة ثلاثاً لثبوت ثلاث حيض في حق المصدقات وأربع حيض في حق المكذبة
اه.
If each one said 'I have menstruated once', each one is divorced one divorce, whether the husband believes her or not, because each one is legally credible regarding what is between her and her husband. And if he said 'Whenever you menstruate, you are divorced' and each one said 'I have menstruated once', then if he disbelieves them all, each one is divorced one divorce because each one's menstruation is established only in respect to herself, not in respect to her co-wives, so for each one only the condition of one divorce exists. And if he believes one but not the other three, then each of the three is divorced twice and the believed one once, because menstruation is established for the believed one but not for her co-wives' menstruation, and for each of the disbelieved ones two menstruations are established: her own by her report and the believed one's by his affirmation. And if he believes two of them, then each believed one is divorced twice (because for each, two menstruations exist: her own and the other believed co-wife's), and each disbelieved one is divorced three times (because for her, three menstruations exist: her own and the two believed ones'). And if he believes all three, each is divorced three times because three menstruations are established for the believed ones and four for the disbelieved one. end.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on conditional divorce when a man addresses his multiple wives saying 'Whenever you menstruate, you are divorced.' The ruling is based on the principle that each woman is legally credible regarding her own menstruation (as established in shar'iah). The husband's belief or disbelief affects the number of divorces. The key is that menstruation is established only in one's own right, not vicariously for others. When the husband believes one wife, her menstruation is established also for the disbelieved wives, increasing the number of divorces for them. This detailed calculation is typical of Hanafi fiqh in conditional divorce cases.

Key Terms
مصدقة (musaddaqa): A wife whose claim of menstruation is believed by the husband.
مكذبة (mukadhdhaba): A wife whose claim of menstruation is disbelieved by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man has four wives and says 'Whenever you menstruate, you are divorced,' and each claims to have menstruated, and he believes two of them, how many divorces does each disbelieved wife receive?
A) 1
B) 2
C) 3
D) 4

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi conditional divorce, each wife's menstruation claim is counted for herself, and the husband's belief extends it to all wives, so the number of divorces per wife equals her own claim plus the number of believed co-wives.

Co-Wife Divorce and Midwife Testimony in Conditional Talaq
Rulings on conditional divorce and testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a conditional divorce on a co-wife occurs and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on midwife testimony.

Core Idea
Conditional divorce on a co-wife depends on husband's knowledge; childbirth testimony is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author discusses two key issues: first, how a husband's knowledge affects divorce on a co-wife when conditioned on her menstruation; second, the evidence required when divorce is conditioned on the wife giving birth. These rulings illustrate important principles about knowledge, testimony, and the limits of what the law can rely upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and knowledge level
Look at the first sentence: the occurrence of divorce on a co-wife depends on the husband's belief if he does not know of her menstruation. But if he knows independently, the divorce falls.
Knowledge here means certain knowledge, not mere suspicion.
2
Distinguish when the husband knows independently vs. only from her
The passage specifies that if the husband knows from other sources (e.g., seeing blood), the divorce depends on his belief or evidence, like entry and speech.
This is by agreement (ittifāqan) of the scholars.
3
Note the agreement on testimony for entry and speech
For internal matters like entry and speech, the ruling hinges on testimony (bayanah) or the husband's acknowledgment, not on the wife's word alone.
This sets a baseline for comparison with menstruation.
4
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on childbirth testimony
When divorce is conditioned on birth, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the midwife's testimony alone, while Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Apply the principle of permission vs. internal states
For actions requiring permission (e.g., drinking, going to father's house), the husband's word is taken if he claims permission, because he denies divorce. This contrasts with internal states like menstruation.
Permission can be proven by speech; internal states cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الوقوع على الضرة لم ينحصر في تصديقه وإنما يتوقف على تصديقه إذا لم يعلم وجود الحيض منها، أما إذا علم طلقت فلانة أيضاً؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وقيد بكونه لا يعلم إلا منها لأنه لو كان يعلم من غيرها توقف الوقوع على تصديقه أو البينة كالدخول والكلام اتفاقاً. واختلفوا فيما لو علق طلاقها بولادتها فقالا يقع الطلاق بشهادة القابلة. وقال الإمام الأعظم : لا بد من شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين كما في الجوهرة. ولا يشمل ما لو علقه على فعل بغير إذنها لما في البزازية : إن شربت مسكراً يغير إذنك فأمرك بيدك وشرب ثم اختلفا في الإذن فالقول له والبينة لها وفي الصيرقية إن ذهبت إلى بيت أبي بغير إذنك فأنت طالق فادعى إذنها وأنكسرت فالقول له لأنه ينكر وقوع الطلاق مع أن الإذن لا يستفاد إلا من قولها ولكن يطلع عليه بالقول بخلاف الحيض والمحبة والبغض ومن قبيل الدخول والكلام ما لو علق بقوله إن كنت جائعة في بيتي قال قاضيخان إن لم تكن جائعة في غير الصوم لا يكون حانثاً. ومنه ما لو علقه بقوله إن لم أشبعك من الجماع قال القاضي : إن جامعها حتى يعرف ما أنزلت فقد أشبعها اهـ. وفي القنية والمسرة كالمحبة وكذا الغيرة باللسان لا بالقلب اهـ. وقد المصنف بين المحبة والحيض وليس بينهما فرق إلا من وجهين: أحدها أن التعليق بالمحبة يقتصر على المجلس لكونه تخييراً حتى لو قامت وقالت أحبك لا تطلق، والتعليق بالحيض لا يبطل بالقيام كسائر التعليقات والثاني أنها إذا كانت كاذبة في الإخبار تطلق في التعليق بالمحبة لما قلنا وفي التعليق بالحيض لا تطلق فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى حتى يحل وطؤها ديانة لأنه حقيقة المحبة والبغض أمر خفي لا يوقف عليها من قبل أحد لا من ولا من قبل غيرها لأن القلب يتقلب لا يستقر على شيء، فلما لم يوقف عليها تعلق الحكم بإخبارها لأنه دليل عليها لأن أحكام الشرع لا تناط بأحكام خفية.
Then know that the occurrence (of divorce) on the co-wife is not confined to his belief; rather it depends on his belief when he does not know the existence of menstruation from her. But if he knows, she is divorced as well; as in al-Jawhara. And it is conditioned that he does not know except from her, because if he knew from other than her, the occurrence would depend on his belief or evidence, as with entry and speech, by agreement. And they differed regarding if he conditioned divorce on her giving birth: the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said divorce occurs by the midwife's testimony. And Imam al-A'zam said: Two men or one man and two women are necessary, as in al-Jawhara. And it does not include when he conditions it on an action without her permission, as in al-Bazzaziyya: 'If you drink an intoxicant without my permission, your affair is in your hand, and she drank, then they differed over permission, then his word is taken and she must provide evidence.' And in al-Sayrakiyya: 'If you go to your father's house without my permission, you are divorced,' and he claimed permission and she denied, then his word is taken because he denies the occurrence of divorce, even though permission can only be known from her statement, but it is learned by speech, unlike menstruation, love, and hatred. And of the type of entry and speech is when he conditions by saying 'If you are hungry in my house,' Qadi Khan said if she is not hungry in other than fasting, he is not an oath-breaker. And of it is when he conditions by saying 'If I do not satisfy you with intercourse,' the Qadi said that if he has intercourse with her until he knows that she has climaxed, then he has satisfied her, end. And in al-Quniyya and al-Masrra, it is like love, and likewise jealousy with the tongue not the heart, end. And the author distinguished between love and menstruation, and there is no difference between them except in two aspects: one is that conditioning on love is confined to the sitting because it is a choice, so that if she stands and says 'I love you' she is not divorced, while conditioning on menstruation is not invalidated by standing like other conditions. The second is that if she is lying in her report, she is divorced in conditioning on love for what we said, and in conditioning on menstruation she is not divorced between herself and Allah Almighty until intercourse becomes permissible for him religiously, because in reality love and hatred are hidden matters that cannot be known from anyone, not from him nor from others, because the heart fluctuates and does not settle on anything. So when it cannot be known, the ruling is attached to her report because it is evidence for it, because the rulings of shari'ah are not attached to hidden matters.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers several important principles in conditional divorce. First, the occurrence of divorce on a co-wife (ضرة) depends on the husband's knowledge: if he knows of her menstruation independently, the divorce falls; otherwise, it depends on his belief in her statement. Second, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding testimony for childbirth: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the midwife's testimony alone, while Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women. Third, when the condition involves an action that requires permission (like entering the father's house), the default rule is that the husband's word is taken regarding permission because the divorce is being denied, even though permission is known only from the wife's statement. This contrasts with menstruation, love, and hatred, which are internal matters. Fourth, the author distinguishes between love and menstruation: love is a choice-based emotion, so if the wife stands up from the sitting where she declared love, the declaration is nullified; menstruation is a physical state that is not affected by movement. Also, if the wife lies about love, the divorce occurs (because the legal effect is tied to her statement), but if she lies about menstruation, the divorce does not occur religiously (between her and Allah), though outwardly the husband can still have intercourse. This is because love is hidden, and the law relies on the outward expression.

Key Terms
الضرة (al-darra): The co-wife; a wife with other wives sharing the same husband.
القابلة (al-qabila): The midwife; a woman present at childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a conditional divorce on a co-wife (al-darra) depend on the husband's belief (tasdiq)?
A) When the husband knows of her menstruation from other sources
B) When the husband does not know of her menstruation except from her
C) When the wife provides evidence of menstruation
D) When the husband denies knowing about menstruation

Key Takeaway
The occurrence of a conditional divorce on a co-wife hinges on the husband's independent knowledge; if he knows from his own observation, the divorce falls automatically.

Distinguishing Love from Menstruation in Conditional Divorce
Distinction between love and menstruation in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two differences between conditioning divorce on love versus on menstruation and apply them to determine when divorce falls.

Core Idea
Love is a choice-based emotion tied to the moment; menstruation is a physical state, so divorce rules differ in continuity and truthfulness.

The author concludes the passage with a crucial distinction between love and menstruation in conditional divorce. Although both are internal states, the law treats them differently because love is emotionally volatile and tied to the utterance, while menstruation is a stable physical condition. Understanding this distinction prevents erroneous applications in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Recognize that both love and menstruation are internal
The text compares love (maḥabbah) and menstruation (ḥayḍ) as hidden matters (umūr khafiyya). Internal states are generally not directly knowable by others.
This is why the law attaches rulings to outward expressions.
2
Note the first difference: confinement to the sitting (majlis)
Conditions on love are considered a choice (takhīr), so the declaration is confined to the sitting. If the wife stands up and declares love again, it does not count.
This does not apply to menstruation; standing does not invalidate the condition.
3
Note the second difference: lying about love vs. menstruation
If the wife lies about love, the divorce occurs (because the ruling is attached to her statement). If she lies about menstruation, the divorce does not occur between her and Allah (diyānan), though outwardly the husband may have intercourse.
The rationale: love is pure emotion; menstruation is a physical state that can be verified.
4
Understand the rationale: love is hidden and changeable
The heart fluctuates (al-qalb yataqallab) and does not settle. Since internal love cannot be known with certainty, the law attaches the ruling to the outward statement.
For menstruation, the ruling is not attached to the statement alone because it can be independently known.
5
Apply to scenarios
Test your understanding by considering variations: e.g., husband says 'If you love me, you are divorced,' wife says 'I love you' but later lies; or husband says 'If you are menstruating,' wife falsely claims menstruation.
The key is whether the condition is based on a temporary emotion or a stable physical state.

المحبة (al-mahabbah): Love; an emotional state considered a choice in conditional divorce.
الحيض (al-hayd): Menstruation; a physical state that is independent of declaration.

Conditional Divorce and Internal States: The Hanafi Principle of Apparent Statement
Rulings on conditional divorce when conditions involve internal states like love, hatred, and pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on conditional divorce based on hidden states and apply the rule that the outward statement is decisive unless there is clear evidence of falsehood or the condition explicitly ties to the heart.

Core Idea
In conditional divorce, hidden states are judged by the outward statement, but if the heart is specified, Muhammad holds the ruling remains with the hidden reality.

When a husband conditions divorce on an internal state like love or hatred, how do we know if the condition is fulfilled? The Hanafi school generally relies on the person's outward statement (zahir), since internal states are hidden. However, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the condition explicitly refers to the heart. This lesson unpacks the rulings from the source and clarifies the practical differences between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of condition
Determine if the condition is tied to a hidden state (love, hatred, pleasure) or an observable act. The ruling differs based on this classification.
Hidden states are judged by the outward statement in general Hanafi principles.
2
Apply the general rule: outward statement governs
For conditions like 'If you love me,' her statement 'I love you' is taken as true both religiously and legally according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because love is an action of the heart expressed by the tongue.
The phrase 'with your heart' is considered mere emphasis by them.
3
Check for explicit heart specification
If the condition explicitly mentions 'with your heart' (e.g., 'If you love me with your heart'), Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that the tongue's substitution is nullified, so the ruling remains attached to the hidden reality. Thus, the divorce does not occur religiously.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: for Muhammad, the husband can have intercourse religiously if he believes she is lying.
4
Consider external evidence of falsehood
When there is apparent evidence of lying (e.g., the husband beats her and she claims she is happy), the outward statement is overruled because we are certain of her falsehood. Her statement is not accepted.
This is contrasted with the torture case where no such evidence exists.
5
Evaluate practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad affects whether he can have intercourse with her religiously. The later preferred view follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, making divorce effective both religiously and legally.
The text states 'الظاهر من كلام مشايخنا' that there is no difference between absolute and tied condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Our master (may Allah be pleased with him) said: In this, happiness is something that cannot be known, so divorce should be attached to her report and her word accepted, even if we are certain of her lie, just as if he said 'If you love that Allah torture you in the fire of hell, you are divorced' and she said 'I love,' divorce occurs upon her; and if he gave a thousand dirhams and she said 'That did not make me happy,' her word is taken and divorce does not occur because it is possible she wanted two thousand, so a thousand does not make her happy. End. An objection and it is: His statement (his statement between them difference) said in al-Nahr: A difference between them may be that the pain of the beating upon her is apparent evidence of her lie, unlike mere love of torture, for there is no evidence for certainty of her lie. His statement (and his statement 'although we').
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage deals with conditional divorce based on internal states: love, hatred, pleasure. The general Hanafi principle is that since these are hidden, the ruling is based on the outward statement (zahir). So if a husband says 'You are divorced if I love such and such' and then falsely denies loving it, he can have intercourse with her religiously because his statement is taken as true in terms of outward rulings. However, Shams al-A'imma finds this problematic because the husband knows his own heart. For love/hate of the wife, Hanafi imams differ: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider that if the wife says 'I love you' (even if conditional on her heart), the divorce occurs both religiously and legally, because the expression suffices. Muhammad says she is not divorced religiously because when the heart is specified, the tongue's substitution is invalidated. The preferred view among later scholars is that there is no difference between love of him or love of separation. The text also discusses extreme cases: if a woman says she loves that Allah torture her in hell, the divorce occurs because her hatred might drive her to lie. Regarding 'If I make you happy,' beating her is considered apparent evidence of her lie, so her statement is not accepted. However, the author (Mawlana) argues that happiness is hidden, so her statement should be accepted despite certainty of falsehood, similar to the torture case. The final part from al-Nahr distinguishes the two cases: in beating, the pain is apparent evidence, so her claim of happiness is clearly false.

Key Terms
ديانة (diyanatan): Religiously; the ruling between the person and Allah, not necessarily enforced in court.
قضاء (qada'an): Legally; the ruling enforced by a judge.
القلب (al-qalb): The heart; the locus of love and intention.
الخلفية (al-khalfiyya): Substitution; the tongue acting as a substitute for the heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In the beating case, the wife is certain to be lying because of external evidence (pain).
B) In the torture case, the wife is certain to be lying because of external evidence.
C) Both cases are treated the same because the condition is on a hidden state.
D) The husband's certainty of lying is the same in both cases.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, conditional divorce on hidden states is generally judged by the outward statement, but explicit mention of the heart triggers Muhammad's view and external evidence of lying can override the statement.

Two Differences Between Ta'liq by Love and by Menstruation
Explaining two differences in rulings between conditional divorce based on love vs menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two differences between ta'liq by love and ta'liq by menstruation and explain the reason for each difference.

Core Idea
Love-based ta'liq is a choice confined to the session; menstruation-based ta'liq is not—and lying has different effects diyanatan.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between conditional divorce based on the wife's love and based on her menstruation. Although both are conditional divorces, two crucial differences affect whether the divorce takes effect and when. Understanding these differences reveals how the law treats internal hidden states versus external observable facts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Highlight the two types of ta'liq: based on love (mahabba) and based on menstruation (hayd). Notice that both are valid conditional divorces.
2
First difference: session confinement
Ta'liq by love is a choice (takhyeer) and is confined to the session. If the wife stands up (leaves the gathering), the condition lapses. Ta'liq by menstruation is not confined; standing does not nullify it.
The key is that love-based ta'liq is treated like an option that must be exercised immediately.
3
Second difference: effect of lying
If the wife lies about her love, she is divorced immediately because the ruling is based on her declaration. But if she lies about menstruation, she is not divorced diyanatan until she actually menstruates.
Diyanatan means between her and Allah; the court may rule differently if there is evidence.
4
Grasp the reason (ta'lil)
Love is a hidden internal state that cannot be known; thus the law relies on her report as evidence. Menstruation is external and observable, so the law requires the actual occurrence.
The heart's changeability makes internal states unreliable for legal attachment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد المصنف بين المحبة والحيض وليس بينهما فرق إلا من وجهين: أحدهما أن التعليق بالمحبة يقتصر على المجلس لكونه تخييراً حتى لو قامت وقالت أحبك لا تطلق، والتعليق بالحيض لا يبطل بالقيام كسائر التعليقات والثاني أنها إذا كانت كاذبة في الإخيار تطلق في التعليق بالمحبة لما قلنا وفي التعليق بالحيض لا تطلق فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى حتى يحل وطؤها ديانة لأنه حقيقة المحبة والبغض أمر خفي لا يوقف عليها من قبل أحد لا من ولا من قبل غيرها لأن القلب يتقلب لا يستقر على شيء، فلما لم يوقف عليها تعلق الحكم بإخبارها لأنه دليل عليها لأن أحكام الشرع لا تناط بأحكام خفية.
The author (al-Hidayah) distinguished between love and menstruation. There is no difference between them except in two respects: one, that ta'liq by love is confined to the session because it is a choice, such that if she stands up and says 'I love you' she is not divorced, while ta'liq by menstruation is not nullified by standing like other ta'liqs. Second, if she is lying in the choice, she is divorced in ta'liq by love as we said, but in ta'liq by menstruation she is not divorced between her and Allah the Exalted until her sexual intercourse becomes permissible diyanatan, because the reality of love and hatred is a hidden matter that cannot be known by anyone, not by her nor by others, because the heart changes and does not settle on anything. Since it cannot be known, the ruling is attached to her report because it is evidence for it, because the rulings of the Sharia are not attached to hidden rulings.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage clarifies two key differences between conditional divorce based on the wife's love (mahabba) versus based on menstruation (hayd). First, ta'liq by love is considered a choice that is specific to the session—if the wife leaves the gathering and then says she loves him, the divorce does not occur, whereas in menstruation-based ta'liq, standing up does not nullify the condition. Second, if the wife lies about her internal state, in love-based ta'liq she is divorced immediately because the ruling is based on her declaration, but in menstruation-based ta'liq she is not divorced between her and Allah (diyanatan) until she actually menstruates, because menstruation is an observable fact. The reason given is that love is a hidden matter of the heart, so the law relies on her report as an indicator, whereas menstruation is manifest and not attached to her report.

Key Terms
التعليق بالمحبة (al-ta'liq bi al-mahabba): A conditional divorce where the husband says 'You are divorced if you love me' or similar
ديانة (diyanatan): Between the person and Allah, not enforceable in court
تخيير (takhyeer): A choice; here it means the wife is given an option that must be exercised immediately in the session

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) She is not divorced because the ta'liq is confined to the session
C) She is divorced only if she menstruates
D) She is divorced diyanatan only

Key Takeaway
Love-based ta'liq is a choice that lapses when the session ends, and the wife's false claim of love triggers divorce, while menstruation-based ta'liq remains until the fact occurs and false claims have no effect diyanatan.

Ta'liq by Internal States: Love and Hatred
Rulings on conditional divorce based on the wife's love or hatred, including truthfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce based on the wife's internal states and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf from Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
In ta'liq by hidden states, the wife's report is binding; specifying 'heart' does not change the majority ruling.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses conditional divorce linked to the wife's love or hatred—internal states that are inherently hidden. Hanafi law relies on the wife's report as the apparent evidence. The text presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute about whether explicitly mentioning 'in your heart' alters the outcome. It also extends the principle to cases involving love for separation or even love for punishment in Hell, illustrating the breadth of the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ta'liq (conditional divorce) where the condition is the wife's internal state (love or hatred). The ruling is that divorce occurs when she reports that state, both diyanatan and qada'an according to the majority.
The husband's own internal state (his love) is treated separately—he knows his own heart.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is that the ruling is attached to the apparent (zahir), which is the wife's report. Since internal states are not knowable with certainty, her statement is taken as evidence.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the impossibility of verifying hidden emotions.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that specifying 'in your heart' does not change the ruling—love is an action of the heart, so the term is merely emphatic. Muhammad argues that the tongue is a substitute for the heart; specifying 'heart' nullifies the substitution, so she is not divorced diyanatan.
The practical difference is that Muhammad's view would allow the husband to maintain the marriage in conscience while he cannot do so legally.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the wife is divorced both diyanatan and qada'an. The mashayikh (later scholars) apparently adopt this view.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Extend to other cases
The rule applies whether the love is for the husband, for separation, or even for punishment in Hell. In all such cases, her report is taken at face value unless the husband is certain of her lying.
The text cites al-Hidayah for the Hellfire example, showing the scope of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage discusses multiple scenarios where divorce is conditioned on the wife's internal state (love or hatred). The key principle is that the ruling is based on the apparent report (zahir), as internal states are hidden. An extreme case is if he conditions on her loving punishment in Hell; here, even without certainty of truth, divorce occurs because she might truly wish for that. This shows that in internal states, the wife's report is taken at face value unless there is certain knowledge of falsehood.

Key Terms
ديانة وقضاء (diyanatan wa qada'an): In religious conscience and in court; binding both before Allah and legally enforceable
خلفية (khilfiyyah): The status of the tongue as a substitute (khalaf) for the heart in expressing internal states
