Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Inheritance After Conditional Divorce with Unconfirmed Hayd
Intra-Hanafi dispute from al-Khaniyya on inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute regarding inheritance when a wife claims menstruation in a conditional divorce, remarries, and the first husband dies.

Core Idea
When the reality of hayd is uncertain, inheritance rights hinge on whether the divorce was effective before consummation.

The final portion of the passage presents a case from al-Khaniyya where a husband said before consummation 'If you menstruate, you are divorced,' the wife claimed menstruation and remarried immediately, then the first husband died. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani gives a ruling that differs from others, causing an intra-madhhab dispute. This lesson dissects that dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the condition
A man says to his wife before consummation: 'If you menstruate, you are divorced.' The wife says 'I menstruated' and marries another man immediately. Then the first husband dies.
The condition is linked to menstruation occurring before consummation.
2
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's ruling
Muhammad says: The inheritance of the woman goes to the first husband, not the second, because it is not known whether the blood was true hayd. Therefore, the divorce before consummation did not occur, and she is still married to the first.
The uncertainty (lack of continuity) prevents the divorce from being established.
3
Identify the opposing position
Other Hanafi scholars (possibly Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf) would likely hold that the wife's claim of menstruation is sufficient for the divorce to take effect, so she is divorced and her second marriage is valid, making the second husband the inheritor.
The text does not name the opponents, but the dispute is implicit.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If Muhammad's view is followed, she inherits from the first husband. If the opposing view, she would inherit from the second husband (if he dies). The disagreement directly impacts the distribution of inheritance.
This is a critical difference that can affect financial rights.
5
Evaluate the basis for Muhammad's doubt
Muhammad says 'It is not known whether that was menstruation or not.' This reflects the principle that hayd requires three days of continuity; since the wife remarried immediately, the continuity cannot be verified, so the condition is unfulfilled.
This reasoning aligns with the earlier rules about continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب التعليق
فقالت
في مسألة إن حضت فعبدي حر وضرتك طالق إذا رأت الدم فقالت حضت وصدقها أنه قبل الاستمرار يمنع الزوج عن وطء المرأة واستخدام العبد في الثلاثة لاحتمال الاستمرار، فلو صدقها الزوج ثم قالت كان الطهر قبل الدم عشرة أيام لم تصدق لأنه بعد إقرارها بالحيض رجوع بخلافه بعد إقرارها برؤية الدم ولو ادعى الزوج أن الدم كان قبله الطهر عشرة أيام وقالت بل عشرين فالقول لها ولو قال وهي حائض إن طهرت فعبدي حر فقالت طهرت بعد ثلاثة أيام وكذبها الزوج لا يعتق وإن صدقها أو مضت العشرة عتق، وإن قالت بعد العشرة عاودني الدم في العشرة وصدقها الزوج وكذبها العبد عتق، وكذا لو قالت ذلك بعدما أقرت بالانقطاع. وإن كان حيضها خمسة فقال لها إن حضت هذه المرة ستة فعبدي حر رأيت الدم في اليوم السادس إلى آخر اليوم وكذبها الزوج فالقول له لإنكاره شرط العتق بخلاف ما إذا علق عتقه بأصل الحيض فادعى الزوج الانقطاع في الثلاث وادعت الامتداد فالقول لها، وإن صدقها الزوج بالدم في اليوم السادس توقف العتق فإن جاوز العشرة تبين أنه لم يكن حيضاً ولم يعتق وإن لم يجاوز عتق فإن مضت فادعت الانقطاع فيها وادعى المجاوزة فالقول له ولا عتق ولو أخبرت في العشرة بالانقطاع ثم قالت عاودني الدم لا يقبل قولها وإن صدقها الزوج، ولو كانت عادتها خمسة فطلقها في مرض موته فحاضت حيضتين الثالثة ثم مات الزوج في بعد خمسة فقالت الورثة طهرت على رأس الخمسة ولا ميراث لك وقالت لم ينقطع وأرى الدم في الحال فالقول لها لأن الأصل في كل ثابت دوامه فهي تتمسك بهذا الظاهر لدفع الحرمان وهو حجة للدفع وتمامه في الكافي. ومن أحكام الوقوع من الابتداء أنها لو كانت غير مدخولة وتزوجت حين رأت الدم فإن النكاح صحيح. ومن أحكامه أنها لا تحسب هذه الحيضة من العدة لأنها بعض حيضة لأنه حين كان الشرط رؤية الدم لزم أن يقع الطلاق بعد حيضها.
وفي الخانية : رجل قال لامرأته قبل الدخول إذا حضت فأنت طالق فقالت حضت وتزوجت من ساعتها ثم مات قال محمد ميراثها للزوج الأول دون الثاني. وقال : لا يدري أكان ذلك حيضاً أو لا ا هـ. ومن أحكامه أيضاً أن الطلاق بدعي. ومنها أنه لو خالعها في الثلاث بطل الخلع لكونها مطلقة ذكرهما في الجوهرة. وفي الثاني نظر لأن الخلع يلحق
قوله : (ثم قالت كان الطهر قبل الدم عشرة أيام أي فلا يكون هذا الدم حيضاً لأن أقل الطهر الفاصل بين الحيضتين خمسة عشر يوماً وقوله بخلافه بعد إقرارها برؤية الدم أي إذا قالت رأيت الدم ولم تقل حضت ثم قالت كان الطهر عشرة أيام فإنها تصدق لأن قولها رأيت الدم ليس إقراراً بالحيض فلم يكن ذلك رجوعاً عن إقرارها قوله: (وفي الثاني نظر الخ) قال في النهر : الظاهر أنه محمول على ما إذا لم تكن مدخولاً بها وعليه فلا إشكال.
[Book of Divorce, Chapter of Conditional Divorce] She said: In the issue: If you menstruate, my slave is free and your co-wife is divorced, when she sees blood and says 'I menstruated' and he confirms her, before continuity it prevents the husband from intercourse with the woman and using the slave in the three [days] due to possibility of continuity. If the husband confirms her, then she says 'the purity before the blood was ten days,' she is not believed because after her acknowledgment of menstruation it is a retraction, contrary to after her acknowledgment of seeing blood. If the husband claims the blood had before it ten days of purity and she says rather twenty, the say is hers. If he says while she is menstruating 'if you become pure, my slave is free,' and she says 'I became pure after three days' and the husband denies her, he is not emancipated; if he confirms her or ten days pass, he is emancipated. If she says after ten days 'the blood returned to me within the ten' and the husband confirms her and the slave denies her, he is emancipated. Likewise if she says that after she acknowledged cessation. If her menstruation is five, and he said to her 'If you menstruate this time six, my slave is free,' she saw blood on the sixth day to the end of the day, and the husband denies her, the say is his because he denies the condition of emancipation, contrary to if he attached emancipation to the origin of menstruation, so the husband claims cessation in the three and she claims extension, the say is hers. If the husband confirms her blood on the sixth day, emancipation is suspended; if it exceeds ten, it becomes clear it was not menstruation and he is not emancipated; if it does not exceed, he is emancipated. If it passes and she claims cessation within it and he claims excess, the say is his and no emancipation. If she reports cessation within the ten then says 'the blood returned to me,' her saying is not accepted even if the husband confirms her. If her custom is five, and he divorces her in his death illness, then she menstruates two menstruations, a third, then the husband dies after five, and the heirs say 'She became pure at the end of five and no inheritance for you,' and she says 'It did not cease and I see blood now,' the say is hers because the principle for every established thing is its continuity; she adheres to this apparent to ward off deprivation, and it is a proof for warding off. Its completion is in al-Kafi. Among the rulings of occurrence from the beginning: if she was not entered upon and she married when she saw the blood, the marriage is valid. Among its rulings: this menstrual period is not counted from the 'iddah because it is part of a menstrual period, because when the condition was seeing blood, it necessitated that divorce falls after her menstruation. In al-Khaniyya: A man said to his wife before consummation 'If you menstruate, you are divorced,' and she said 'I menstruated' and married immediately, then he died. Muhammad said: Her inheritance is for the first husband, not the second. And he said: It is not known whether that was menstruation or not. End. Among its rulings also: the divorce is bid'i. Among them: if he made khul' with her in the three, the khul' is invalid because she is divorced, mentioned in al-Jawhara. In the second there is consideration because khul' attaches to... His saying: (Then she said the purity before the blood was ten days) meaning this blood is not menstruation because the minimum purity separating two menstruations is fifteen days. And his saying: contrary to after her acknowledgment of seeing blood, meaning if she said 'I saw blood' and did not say 'I menstruated,' then said 'the purity was ten days,' she is believed because her saying 'I saw blood' is not an acknowledgment of menstruation, so that was not a retraction of her acknowledgment. His saying: (And in the second there is consideration etc.) He said in al-Nahr: The apparent is that it is carried on if she was not entered upon, and thus there is no problem.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of rulings from Kanz al-Daqa'iq on conditional divorce linked to menstruation. It opens by presenting a case where a husband says 'If you menstruate, my slave is free and your co-wife is divorced.' The wife claims she saw blood and menstruated. If the husband confirms her, before the blood is confirmed as hayd by continuity (lasting three days), he is prevented from intercourse and using the slave due to possibility that the blood may not be true menstruation. The author then discusses retraction: if after confirming she later says her purity before the blood was ten days (which would negate hayd because the minimum purity is fifteen days), she is not believed because she already acknowledged hayd. But if she only said she saw blood, not that she menstruated, her subsequent claim of ten-day purity is accepted. In cases of disagreement about the length of purity before blood, or the number of days of bleeding, the say is given to the woman in some scenarios and to the husband in others, based on who is denying the condition for emancipation. The text also covers the scenario where a woman's habit is five days but condition is set for six; if she sees blood on the sixth day and husband denies, the husband's say prevails because he denies the condition. If he confirms, emancipation is suspended until it is known whether the bleeding exceeds ten days. The passage also addresses inheritance in a death-illness divorce, where the principle of continuity (istishab) is applied to accept the woman's claim that she is still menstruating, inheriting from her husband. Later, rulings about the validity of marriage if she is non-madkhula and marries immediately, and that this type of divorce is bid'i (innovative). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute from al-Khaniyya where Muhammad holds inheritance goes to first husband, and a comment that khul' during the three days is invalid because she is already divorced. The commentary then explains the matn: the wife's retraction is not accepted after she says 'I menstruated' but is accepted if she only said 'I saw blood'. The passage ends by noting a consideration on the second point about khul'.

Key Terms
خانية (al-Khāniyya): A Hanafi fatwa collection attributed to Imam Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi al-Farghani (d. 592 AH), containing nawadir and fatwa cases.
ميراث (mīrāth): Inheritance rights; in this context, the woman inherits from her husband upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the wife admitted she lied about menstruation.
B) Because the condition of the divorce (hayd) was not verified with certainty.
C) Because the second marriage was invalid due to lack of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
When the fulfillment of a conditional divorce is uncertain, the legal status quo (original marriage) is preserved, affecting inheritance rights.

The Four Methods for Establishing Rulings: Iqtisar, Inqilab, Istinad, and Tabayyun
Classifies and explains the four ways conditional divorces take effect: immediate, retroactive, and revelatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four methods (iqtisar, inqilab, istinad, tabayyun) and apply them to conditional divorce scenarios.

Core Idea
Rulings take effect either instantly (iqtisar, inqilab) or retroactively (istinad, tabayyun); the key distinction is human knowability.

In Hanafi fiqh, the timing of a ruling's effect is critical, especially in conditional divorce. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq classifies how rulings are established through four methods: iqtisar, inqilab, istinad, and tabayyun. Understanding these categories helps determine when a divorce actually occurs and the start of the 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four methods
The passage opens by listing iqtisar, inqilab, istinad, and tabayyun. Recognize that they represent two categories: immediate (iqtisar, inqilab) and retroactive (istinad, tabayyun).
These are not mutually exclusive; istinad shares features with tabayyun but differs in knowability.
2
Examine iqtisar and inqilab
Iqtisar: the ruling is created directly at the moment of utterance (e.g., 'you are divorced now'). Inqilab: a condition transforms something not a cause into a cause at the time the condition is fulfilled (e.g., 'if you enter, you are divorced').
Iqtisar is the default for explicit declarations; inqilab applies to conditional phrases.
3
Examine istinad and tabayyun
Istinad: the ruling is established in the present but assigned to an earlier time, but that earlier state is unknowable to people (e.g., zakat on nisab assigned to start of year). Tabayyun: the ruling is revealed to have been in effect from an earlier time, but that earlier state could theoretically be known (e.g., if menstruation is later confirmed by three days).
The passage uses the hayd example: divorce is judged from the start of menstruation only after three days confirm it.
4
Distinguish istinad from tabayyun
The key difference: tabayyun's prior state can be known by people (e.g., by cutting open the womb to confirm blood origin), while istinad's cannot. Also, locality (mahalliyya) is required for istinad but not for tabayyun, and istinad only affects existing things, while tabayyun affects both existing and perished.
This distinction is crucial for determining the start of 'iddah and the effect of intermediate acts.
5
Apply to the 'one month before death' example
The passage analyzes: 'You are divorced one month before the death of so-and-so.' If the person dies exactly one month later, the divorce is by istinad, assigned to one month before. This means the 'iddah starts from that earlier time, and acts like intercourse or khul' during the month have legal consequences.
If he says 'before arrival' instead, it is iqtisar, not istinad, so the divorce only takes effect at arrival.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطلاق الصريح كما قدمناه في آخر باب الكنايات. وذكر المؤلف في المستصفى من باب المسح على الخفين الأحكام تثبت بطرق أربعة : الاقتصار كما إذا أنشأ الطلاق أو العتاق وله نظائر جمة، والانقلاب وهو انقلاب ما ليس بعلة علة كما إذا علق الطلاق أو العتاق بالشرط فعند وجود الشرط ينقلب ما ليس بعلة علة . والاستناد أن وهو يثبت في الحال ثم يستند وهو دائر بين التبيين والاقتصار وذلك كالمضمونات تملك عند أداء الضمان مستنداً إلى وقت وجود السبب، وكالنصاب فإنه يجب الزكاة عند تمام الحول مستنداً إلى وقت وجوده، وكالطهارة في المستحاضة والتيمم ينقض عند خروج الوقت ورؤية الماء مستنداً إلى وقت الحدث، ولذا قلنا : لا يجوز المسح لهما والتبيين وهو أن يظهر في الحال أن الحكم كان ثابتاً من قبل مثل أن يقول في اليوم إن كان زيد في الدار فأنت طالق وتبين في الغد وجوده فيها فيقع الطلاق في اليوم ويعتبر ابتداء العدة منه، وكما إذا قال لامرأته إذا حضت فأنت طالق فرأت الدم لا يقضي بوقوع الطلاق ما لم يمتد ثلاثة أيام، فإذا امتد ثلاثة أيام حكمنا بوقوع الطلاق من حين حاضت. والفرق بين التبيين والاستناد أن التبيين يمكن أن يطلع عليه العباد وفي الاستناد لا يمكن، وفي الحيض يمكن أن يطلع عليه بأن يشق بطنها فيعلم أنه من الرحم. وكذا يشترط المحلية في الاستناد دون التبيين وكذا الاستناد يظهر أثره في القائم دون المتلاشي، وأثر التبيين يظهر فيهما فلو قال أنت طالق قبل موت فلان بشهر لم تطلق حتى يموت فلان اليمين بشهر ، فإن مات لتمام الشهر طلقت مستنداً إلى أول الشهر فتعتبر العدة من أوله. ولو وطئها في الشهر صار مراجعاً لو كان الطلاق رجعياً وغرم العقر لو كان بائناً، ويرد الزوج بدل الخلع إليها لو خالعها في خلاله ثم مات فلان ولو مات فلان بعد العدة بأن كانت بالوضع أو لم تجب العدة لكونه قبل الدخول لا يقع الطلاق لعدم المحل. وبهذا تبين أنه فيها بطريق الاستناد لا بطريق التبيين وهو الصحيح، ولو قال أنت طالق قبل قدوم فلان بشهر يقع مقتصراً على القدوم لا مستنداً ا هـ.
Explicit divorce as we presented at the end of the chapter on kinayat. The author mentioned in al-Mustasfa from the chapter of wiping over the socks that rulings are established by four methods: 1) al-Iqtisar (summary) as when one initiates divorce or emancipation, and it has many analogues. 2) al-Inqilab (transformation) which is the transformation of what is not a cause into a cause, as when one attaches divorce or emancipation to a condition, then upon existence of the condition, what was not a cause becomes a cause. 3) al-Istinad (retroactive assignment) which is that [the ruling] is established in the present then is assigned retroactively, and it revolves between tabayyun and iqtisar. That is like the guaranteed things: one owns upon payment of the guarantee assigned back to the time of the cause, and like the nisab: zakat becomes obligatory upon completion of the year assigned back to the time of its existence, and like purity in the mustahada and tayammum: they are nullified at the exit of time and seeing water assigned back to the time of the hadath. Therefore we said: wiping is not permissible for them. 4) al-Tabayyun (revelation) which is that it appears in the present that the ruling was established from before. Like if he says today 'If Zayd is in the house, you are divorced,' and it becomes clear the next day that he was in it, then the divorce falls today and the beginning of the 'iddah is considered from it. And like if he said to his wife 'If you menstruate, you are divorced,' and she sees blood, it is not judged that the divorce occurs unless it extends three days. When it extends three days, we judge that the divorce occurred from the time she menstruated. The difference between tabayyun and istinad is that tabayyun can be known by people, while istinad cannot. In menstruation, it can be known by cutting open her belly to know it is from the womb. Likewise locality is required in istinad but not in tabayyun. Likewise istinad shows its effect in what is existing, not in what has perished, while the effect of tabayyun appears in both. So if he says 'You are divorced one month before the death of so-and-so,' she is not divorced until so-and-so dies? [The text has 'اليمين' maybe a typo] then if he dies at the completion of the month, she is divorced assigned back to the beginning of the month, so the 'iddah is calculated from its beginning. If he had intercourse with her during the month, he becomes a returner if the divorce was revocable, and he pays the 'uqr if it was irrevocable, and the husband returns the khul' compensation to her if he made khul' with her during it, then so-and-so died. And if so-and-so dies after the 'iddah, whether by delivery or no 'iddah due to before consummation, the divorce does not occur due to lack of subject. By this it becomes clear that it is by way of istinad, not tabayyun, and that is the correct view. And if he says 'You are divorced one month before the arrival of so-and-so,' it falls limited to the arrival, not by istinad. End.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a theoretical framework for how legal rulings, especially divorce, are established through four methods: iqtisar, inqilab, istinad, and tabayyun. Iqtisar is the direct creation of the ruling at the moment of utterance. Inqilab is when a condition transforms something that is not a cause into a cause. Istinad is retroactive assignment: the ruling is established in the present but is considered to have been in effect from an earlier time. Tabayyun is when the ruling is revealed to have been in effect from an earlier time based on evidence that becomes known later. The author gives detailed examples: for istinad, guarantee contracts, zakat on nisab at end of year, and purity of mustahada. The treatment of conditional divorce with hayd is used to illustrate tabayyun: divorce is judged to have occurred from the beginning of hayd only after three days confirm it, but this is actually tabayyun because the fact becomes known later. The passage distinguishes istinad from tabayyun: istinad applies to matters that cannot be known by people (like internal states), while tabayyun applies to matters that can be known. Locality (mahalliyya) is required for istinad but not tabayyun. The example of 'You are divorced one month before the death of so-and-so' is analyzed: it is by istinad, so if the person dies exactly after a month, the divorce is assigned to the start of the month. But if he says 'before the arrival of so-and-so,' it is iqtisar, not istinad. This shows the practical difference: with istinad, acts done during the interim (like intercourse, khul') affect the legal status.

Key Terms
الاقتصار (al-iqtisār): The direct creation of a legal ruling at the moment of utterance without retroactive effect.
الانقلاب (al-inqilāb): Transformation: a condition causes something that is not a cause to become a cause at the time the condition is fulfilled.
الاستناد (al-istinād): Retroactive assignment: the ruling is established in the present but considered to have been in effect from an earlier time.
التبيين (al-tabayyun): Revelation: a ruling is revealed to have been in effect from a prior time based on knowledge that becomes apparent later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced one month before the death of so-and-so.' If so-and-so dies exactly one month later, what method applies and when is the 'iddah calculated from?
A) Iqtisar; 'iddah from the moment of utterance
B) Inqilab; 'iddah from the death
C) Istinad; 'iddah from the beginning of the month (one month before death)
D) Tabayyun; 'iddah from the death

Key Takeaway
The four methods—iqtisar, inqilab, istinad, tabayyun—govern when a conditional divorce takes effect; the critical divide is between immediate/transformative (iqtisar, inqilab) and retroactive/revelatory (istinad, tabayyun).

Conditional Divorce on Menstruation: Occurrence and Report Requirement
Explains the conditional divorce ruling and introduces an intra-madhhab dispute about the wife's report at purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a conditional divorce using the phrase 'if you menstruate one menstruation' takes effect, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute about the wife's report.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce on menstruation occurs upon complete purity, but later authorities require the wife's report for it to take effect.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a conditional divorce tied to the wife's menstruation. The matn states that the divorce falls upon purity, but a later fatwa source introduces a key requirement: the wife must report her purity at the time. Understanding this dispute clarifies how conditional oaths operate in Hanafi fiqh and highlights the evolution of fatwa within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrase and ruling
The husband says 'if you menstruate one menstruation, you are divorced.' The matn says the divorce falls when she becomes pure. Note the ruling is conditional and valid.
2
Define complete menstruation and purity
'Haydah' means a complete menstruation (minimum 3 days, max 10). Purity is either by passing ten days or cessation of blood with assuming rulings of purity.
Analogy to fasting a day: a partial fast does not count.
3
Understand the analogy to other conditional oaths
Similar phrases like 'if you fast a day' or 'pray a prayer' require full completion. The same applies to menstruation: partial does not fulfill the condition.
4
Examine the apparent meaning of the matn regarding reporting
The matn says 'but when she becomes pure, it falls', which seems to imply no further report is needed. This is the apparent view.
5
Explore the later Hanafi view requiring report
Al-TatarKhaniyya, quoting al-Dhakhira and al-Jami', states that divorce does not occur unless the wife reports at purity after the completion of the menstruation. This is the mufta bihi position.
The report is needed because the condition is known only to the wife.

Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a conditional divorce using the phrase 'if you menstruate one menstruation.' It explains that the divorce occurs when she becomes pure, meaning either after the full ten days if the bleeding continues that long, or upon cessation of blood if it stops before ten days and she assumes the rulings of a pure woman (like being allowed to pray and fast) because 'a menstruation' linguistically means a complete one. The author analogizes to other conditional oaths like 'if you fast a day' – one is not considered to have fasted unless he completes a full day, similarly, a complete menstruation is required. The comment then addresses the matn's phrase 'but when she becomes pure, it falls,' which seems to indicate no need for her to report her purity again. However, the author cites from al-TatarKhaniyya quoting al-Dhakhira and al-Jami' that the divorce does not occur unless she reports at the time of purity after the completion of the menstruation, because her report is about the condition being fulfilled at that moment. The passage ends with the matn 'She is not believed until...' which likely continues with conditions for her report.

Key Terms
الحيضة (al-ḥayḍah): A complete menstruation; required for the condition to be fulfilled in a conditional divorce like 'if you menstruate one menstruation'.
الطهر (al-ṭuhr): Purity from menstruation; the time when the divorce takes effect in the phrase 'if you menstruate one menstruation'.
الإخبار (al-ikhbār): The wife's report of her purity; according to some later Hanafi authorities, this report is necessary for the divorce to occur.

When Does a Conditional Divorce Linked to Menstruation Occur?
Details the timing and conditions of conditional divorce with menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a divorce conditional upon menstruation occurs, and distinguish between the roles of the wife's testimony and the condition of purification.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce linked to menstruation requires a complete haydah followed by purification — the divorce falls upon purity, not upon seeing blood.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the timing of a divorce made conditional on the wife's menstruation. The central issue is understanding what constitutes a complete menstruation (haydah) and when the divorce actually takes effect. Additionally, the text addresses how the wife's statement about her state is evaluated, balancing trust with the risk of delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrase and its basic ruling
The matn states: 'If you menstruate a menstruation, it falls when you become pure.' This means the divorce occurs after a complete menstruation and subsequent purification, not upon mere blood flow.
The key phrase is 'hina tathuru' (when she becomes pure).
2
Define 'haydah' — a complete menstruation
The commentator explains that 'haydah' (with fatha) means a single complete menstrual period, defined either by the passage of ten days or by cessation of blood with signs of purity if less than ten. Fractional terms like half a haydah do not trigger divorce.
This distinguishes haydah (occasion) from hayd (noun, kasra) meaning the genus.
3
Distinguish between 'bi-haydati' and 'fi haydatik'
The phrase 'bi-haydati' (with your menstruation) refers to a specific occasion, requiring a complete haydah. 'Fi haydatik' (in your menstruation) indicates the genus, like saying 'if you pray', and does not require completeness.
The distinction affects whether fractions or incomplete acts fulfill the condition.
4
Apply the wife's testimony rules
The wife is believed if she reports promptly (within a plausible time after the event). If she delays, her word is not accepted until she purifies, because delay implies suspicion of falsehood.
Timely announcement is crucial: 'al-qawl laha idha akhbarat fi awaniha'.
5
Note the nuance of future vs. present menstruation
If the husband knows she is currently menstruating when he makes the oath, the condition refers to a future menstruation, not the current one, unless he specifically intended continuation.
This prevents double use of the same menstruation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والحال منافية لما أخبرت ا.هـ. وفي تلخيص الجامع للصدر : من الإنشاء ملك الإخبار كالوصي والمولى والمراجع والوكيل بالبيع ومن له الخيار. قال إذا حضت حيضة فأنت طالق فقال بعد مدة محتملة حضت وطهرت وقع، ولو المستقبل ومرض في المستقبل، فإن نوى ما يحدث من هذا الحيض أو ما يزيد من هذا المرض فهو كما نوى، وكذا إذا قال لصاحبة الرعاف إن رعفت، وكذا إذا قال للحبلى إذا حبلت فهو على حبل في المستقبل، ولو تحيض) أي ولا Likewise if he said 'half a menstruation' or 'a third of it' or 'a sixth of it' or 'you are divorced with your menstruation' or 'in your menstruation' with ta, like his saying 'If you fast a day' or 'you prayed a prayer', he does not break his oath except by fasting a complete day and with shaf' (intercession?) contrary to what preceded because it indicates the genus of menstruation, so it is like his saying 'If you fast' or 'you prayed'. And he indicated by his statement: His statement: (But if she becomes pure, it falls) apparently means that there is no need for a second announcement at the time of purity, but in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Dhakhira from al-Jami': The divorce does not occur except if she announces at the time of purity after the conclusion of this menstruation; then the divorce occurs due to her announcement of what is the condition for the occurrence of divorce at the time of its existence. His statement: (She is not believed until she announces) She possesses 'when she becomes pure' to the effect that it is not bid'i. And he indicated by his statement 'when she saw blood' that it is bid'i, and that if she was menstruating, she is not divorced until she becomes pure and then menstruates, like his saying to a pure woman 'If you become pure then you are divorced' - she is not divorced until she menstruates then becomes pure, because we have established that the oath requires a future condition. And in al-Sihah: al-haydah with fatha is the single occasion, and al-haydah with kasra is the noun, plural hayd. In al-Khaniyya: If he said to her while she was menstruating 'If you menstruate then you are divorced', it refers to future menstruation; and if he said to her 'If you menstruate tomorrow then you are divorced' while knowing she is menstruating, it refers to the continuation of that menstruation until tomorrow - if it continues until tomorrow dawns, she is divorced because a second menstruation cannot occur from tomorrow, so it is interpreted as continuation when he knows. In al-Kafi: If she said after ten days 'I menstruated and became pure' and her husband denied her, she is divorced because she is trustworthy in her time; and if she said after a month 'I menstruated and became pure, then I menstruated another menstruation and I am now menstruating', her statement is not accepted, but if she becomes pure, it occurs because she delayed the announcement from its time and thus becomes suspect. And if he said 'If you menstruate then you are divorced' and she said after five days 'I menstruated and I am menstruating now', her word is accepted because the announcement is in its time; and if she said 'I menstruated and became pure', she is not believed until she menstruates because she announced a situation contradictory to what she announced. In Talkhis al-Jami' li al-Sadr: From the perspective of creation, one possesses the authority to inform like the executor, the master, the retractor, the agent for sale, and one who has an option. He said: If she said 'I menstruated a menstruation and became pure', it occurs; and if she said 'I menstruated and became pure and I am menstruating', not until she becomes pure; and if he said 'If you menstruate' and she said 'I menstruated five days ago', it occurs and she is not suspect in delay due to excuse; and if she said 'and became pure', no. And mentioned in the chapter on oath-breaking that menstruation and action occur: He said 'You are divorced one month before you menstruate a menstruation' and she menstruated afterwards, she is divorced and one does not wait for purity due to separation, and they differed, and the most correct is that it is limited. And if he said 'one month before the arrival of so-and-so or the death of so-and-so' and arrival preceded, it occurs; but death does not, contrary to if he said 'if he arrives or dies' due to the conditional. In al-Jawhara: If she menstruates half a menstruation then she is divorced, and if she menstruates the other half then she is divorced, nothing occurs until she menstruates and becomes pure; so if she menstruates and becomes pure, two divorces occur. And if he said to her while she is menstruating 'If you menstruate then you are divorced' or said while she is sick 'If you become sick' - this refers to future menstruation and future sickness; if he intended what happens from this menstruation or what increases from this sickness, it is as he intended. Likewise if he said to a woman with epistaxis 'If you bleed', and likewise if he said to a pregnant woman 'If you become pregnant' - it refers to future pregnancy. And 'she menstruates' means it does not depend on purity because the speech concerns when he said to her 'If you menstruate' contrary to what passed, for if she announces her second menstruation, it is not accepted until she becomes pure because she is being descriptive in the case where he said 'If you menstruate a menstruation' which is the name for a complete one. Consider his statement: (Contrary to if he said 'if he arrives' or 'dies' - apparently 'ma' is redundant or there is a lacuna, and the original is 'contrary to if he said if he arrives or dies' - let it be referred back.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq provides detailed rulings on conditional divorce linked to menstruation. The commentator explains the matn's phrase 'if you menstruate a menstruation, it falls when you become pure'. This means the divorce occurs only after a complete menstruation (defined as either the passage of ten days or cessation of blood with signs of purity if less than ten) and subsequent purification. The term 'haydah' refers to a complete menstruation, so fractions like half a haydah do not trigger divorce. The commentator distinguishes between the phrase 'with your menstruation' (bi-haydati) and 'in your menstruation' (fi haydatik); the latter indicates genus, similar to saying 'if you pray' without specifying a complete prayer. The text then addresses the wife's testimony: if she reports menstruation and purity within a plausible time, she is believed; but if she delays, she becomes suspect. There is a discussion of whether divorce occurs at the moment of menstruation or upon purification. The dominant view is that it occurs upon purification, not upon seeing blood, to avoid association with bid'ah (innovative) divorce. The passage also covers cases where the husband explicitly knows she is menstruating at the time of the oath, in which case the condition refers to future menstruation. Other scenarios include multiple conditional divorces tied to halves of a haydah, and divorce before a specific time (like a month before menstruation). The text quotes many Hanafi sources (al-Kafi, al-Khaniyya, al-Jawhara, etc.) showing the richness of the school's discourse.

Key Terms
حيضة (بالفتح) (haydah (with fatha)): The single occurrence of menstruation; the complete menstrual period that triggers the ruling.
حيضة (بالكسر) (haydah (with kasra)): The noun form meaning menstruation as a concept; used in phrases like 'fi haydatik'.
البدعي (al-bid'i): Innovative; a type of divorce that is considered blameworthy. Here, divorce that occurs during menstruation is bid'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A conditional divorce tied to menstruation requires a complete haydah and purification; the divorce falls at purification, not at the onset of blood.

Conditional Divorce During Menstruation: Future vs. Continuation
Ruling on conditional divorce for a menstruating woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two scenarios of conditional divorce for a menstruating woman and apply the Hanafi principle that a condition in an oath must be future.

Core Idea
A condition in a divorce oath must refer to a future event; if future is impossible, it refers to continuation.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school interprets a husband's conditional divorce statement when the wife is already menstruating. The central question is whether the condition 'if you menstruate' refers to the current menstruation or a future one. We will explore two scenarios: a general condition and a time-bound condition, and apply the rule that an oath requires a future possibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First scenario: husband says to his menstruating wife 'if you menstruate, you are divorced.' Second scenario: he says 'if you menstruate tomorrow' while knowing she is menstruating. Recognize the difference in wording.
2
Apply the principle of future condition
Recall the Hanafi rule: an oath (yameen) requires a future condition. The condition cannot be a present or past state. Apply this to the first scenario: the current menstruation cannot serve as the condition, so it must refer to a future menstruation after the current one ends.
The principle is mentioned in the passage: 'al-yameen taqtadi shartan mustaqbalan.'
3
Interpret the linguistic phrase
Consider the definition of 'haydah' (single menstruation) vs. 'hayd' (noun). The condition uses 'haydah' implying a single occurrence. In the time-bound scenario, 'tomorrow' is specified, but a new menstruation cannot occur tomorrow because she is already menstruating. Thus, the condition is interpreted as the continuation of the current menstruation until tomorrow.
Refer to al-Sihah for the linguistic distinction.
4
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For the general condition: divorce occurs when she becomes pure from the current menstruation and then menstruates again (a future haydah). For the time-bound condition: divorce occurs if the current menstruation persists until dawn tomorrow, because continuation is the only possible interpretation.
The passage explicitly states these rulings.
5
Note the practical consequence
The timing of divorce differs. In the general condition, the divorce is delayed possibly weeks. In the time-bound condition, it occurs the next morning if menstruation continues. This affects the wife's waiting period and rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أشار بقوله حين رأت الدم إلى أنه بدعي وإلى أنها لو كانت حائضاً لا تطلق ما لم تطهر ثم تحيض كقوله لطاهرة إذا طهرت فأنت طالق لم تطلق حتى تحيض ثم تطهر لما قدمنا أن اليمين تقتضي شرطاً مستقبلاً. وفي الصحاح : الحيضة بالفتح المرة الواحدة والحيضة بالكسر الاسم والجمع الحيض. وفي الخانية : لو قال لها وهي حائض إذا حضت فأنت طالق فهو على حيض في المستقبل، ولو قال لها إن حضت غداً فأنت طالق وهو يعلم أنها حائض فهو على دوام ذلك الحيض إلى الغد إن دام إلى أن يطلع الغد طلقت لأن الحيضة الثانية لا يتصور حدوثها من الغد فيحمل على الدوام إذا علم.
He indicated by his saying 'when she sees blood' that it is an innovation, and that if she was menstruating, she is not divorced until she becomes pure and then menstruates, like his saying to a pure woman 'if you become pure, you are divorced' – she is not divorced until she menstruates and then becomes pure, because we have established that an oath requires a future condition. In al-Sihah: al-haydah (with fatha on ha) is the single instance, and al-haydah (with kasra on ha) is the noun, and the plural is hayd. In al-Khaniyah: if he said to her while she is menstruating 'if you menstruate, you are divorced', it refers to future menstruation; and if he said to her 'if you menstruate tomorrow, you are divorced', while knowing that she is menstruating, it refers to the continuation of that menstruation until tomorrow – if it lasts until tomorrow dawns, she is divorced, because a second menstruation cannot occur tomorrow, so it is interpreted as continuation when he knows.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on conditional divorce involving menstruation. It addresses two scenarios: first, when a husband says to his menstruating wife 'if you menstruate, you are divorced' – this refers to a future menstruation, not the current one, because an oath requires a future condition. Second, if he says 'if you menstruate tomorrow' while she is already menstruating, it refers to the continuation of the current menstruation until tomorrow, since a new menstruation cannot occur tomorrow. The passage also defines the term 'haydah' (menstruation) linguistically. The authority weight is from al-Khaniyah, which is a later Hanafi fatwa collection, but the principle is consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الحيضة (al-haydah): A single instance of menstruation; used as the condition for divorce.
اليمين (al-yameen): An oath or conditional statement that triggers a legal consequence.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect on the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A husband's conditional divorce statement to a menstruating wife must be interpreted as referring to a future menstruation, unless a specific time is mentioned, in which case it refers to continuation.

Ruling on Conditional Divorce: 'Before a Menstruation by a Month'
Ruling on conditional divorce worded as 'before a month's menstruation'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a conditional divorce tied to a future menstrual period, explain why purity is not required for immediate separation, and distinguish between conditions based on arrival versus death.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce may take effect immediately upon the condition's fulfillment, without waiting for purity.

In Hanafi fiqh, conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq) is valid and takes effect when the condition is fulfilled. However, the nature of the condition affects the outcome. This lesson analyzes a specific condition phrased as 'before a month's menstruation' and contrasts it with conditions tied to someone's arrival or death. Understanding these nuances prevents legal errors in divorce pronouncements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition phrase
Examine the wording: 'You are divorced before you menstruate a menstruation by a month.' Note that the condition is a future event (menstruation) with a time frame (by a month).
The time frame 'by a month' sets the outer limit; if menstruation occurs within that month, the condition is fulfilled.
2
Determine the ruling upon menstruation
When she menstruates after a month (i.e., within the condition's scope), the divorce occurs immediately. The text states: 'she is divorced' (taliq) at that moment.
No further delay; the divorce is effective upon the start of menstruation.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on waiting for purity
Some Hanafi scholars hold that the divorce only takes effect after she becomes pure from that menstruation. However, the relied-upon view ('al-asahh') is that purity is not required because the divorce here is irrevocable (baynunah).
The logic: waiting for purity is only relevant for revocable divorces where reconciliation is possible; here, immediate separation makes waiting unnecessary.
4
Distinguish between arrival and death conditions
If the condition is 'before Zaid's arrival by a month', and Zaid arrives, divorce occurs. But if the condition is 'before Zaid's death by a month', and he dies, divorce does not occur. The reason is that arrival is a predictable event that can be 'before' with a time limit, but death is not an event that can be anticipated in that way.
The conditional wording requires a potential for the event to occur 'before' the time limit; death is considered inevitable but not predictable within a fixed timeframe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في باب الحنث يقع الحيض والفعل : قال أنت طالق قبل أن تحيضي حيضة بشهر فحاضت بعده طلقت ولا ينتظر الطهر للبينونة واختلفوا، والأصح فيه أنه يقتصر. ولو قال قبل قدوم فلان أو موت فلان بشهر وتقدم القدوم يقع والموت لا بخلاف ما إذا قدم ومات للتعليق.
And it is mentioned in the chapter of breaking the oath: menstruation and the action occur. He said: 'You are divorced before you menstruate a menstruation by a month' – she menstruated after that, she is divorced, and purity is not waited for separation, and they differed, and the most correct is that it is limited. And if he said 'before the arrival of Zaid or the death of Zaid by a month' and the arrival occurs, it occurs; concerning death, no, unlike if he arrived and died, because of the conditional wording.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage discusses a conditional divorce where the husband says 'you are divorced before you menstruate a menstruation by a month'. If she then menstruates after a month, she is divorced immediately upon menstruation; the waiting for purity after menstruation is not required for separation (baynunah). There is disagreement, but the most correct view is that it is limited to the condition. The passage also contrasts conditional divorce tied to arrival versus death: if he says 'before Zaid's arrival by a month' and Zaid arrives, divorce occurs; but if he says 'before Zaid's death by a month' and Zaid dies, divorce does not occur because death is not an event that can be anticipated like arrival. The ruling hinges on the nature of the condition.

Key Terms
الحنث (al-hanath): Breaking an oath; here refers to the fulfillment of the condition causing divorce.
البينونة (al-baynūnah): Separation; the divorce that makes the wife irrevocably divorced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'You are divorced before you menstruate a menstruation by a month.' She menstruates after a month. According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, when does the divorce take effect?
A) Immediately upon menstruation.
B) After she becomes pure from that menstruation.
C) One month after the statement.
D) The divorce is invalid because the wording is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
In conditional divorce, the nature of the condition determines the ruling: predictable events trigger immediate divorce, while death does not, and purity is not required for irrevocable separations.

Wife's Testimony on Menstruation: Timeliness Required
Rulings on wife's testimony about menstruation in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a wife's testimony about her menstruation is accepted in conditional divorce and apply the rule of timeliness.

Core Idea
A wife is trusted about her menstruation only if she reports promptly; delay raises suspicion.

This lesson examines when a wife's word about her menstruation is accepted in the context of a conditional divorce. The Hanafi school grants her trustworthiness (amana) in matters of hayd and iddah, but this trust is conditional upon timely reporting. We will work through the text from al-Kafi and Talkhis al-Jami' al-Sadr to understand the precise boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The wife is considered amana (trustworthy) regarding her own menstruation, but only 'fi awaniha' (in its proper time). Timeliness is key.
This principle sets the baseline: she is believed unless she delays.
2
Apply to immediate reporting
If she reports within a plausible time (e.g., five or ten days), her word is accepted, even if the husband denies.
Example: 'If you menstruate, you are divorced' and she says after five days 'I am menstruating now' is accepted.
3
Apply to delayed reporting
If she delays significantly (e.g., a month), her claim of current menstruation is not accepted because she becomes suspected (mutahama). The divorce will only occur when she actually becomes pure.
Delayed report loses trustworthiness; she must produce evidence.
4
Distinguish contradictory claims
If she claims both menstruation and purity at the same time, she is not believed until she actually menstruates, because the claim contradicts her present state.
Example: saying 'I menstruated and became pure and am now menstruating' is contradictory if she is currently menstruating?
5
Extend to other trustees
The rule of trustworthiness also applies to those who have authority over legal effects, like executors, agents, and holders of options.
They are trusted in their reports within their sphere of authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الكافي : لو قالت بعد عشرة أيام حضت وظهرت وكذبها الزوج تطلق لأنها الأمانة في أوانها، ولو قالت بعد مضي شهر إني حضت وطهرت ثم حضت حيضة أخرى وأنا الآن حائض لا يقبل قولها، ولكن إذا طهرت يقع لأنها أخرت الإخبار عن أوانه فصارت متهمة. ولو قال إذا حضت فأنت طالق فقالت بعد خمسة أيام حضت وأنا حائض الساعة فالقول لها لأن الإخبار في أوانه، ولو قالت حضت وطهرت لا تصدق حتى تحيض لأنها أخبرت والحال منافية لما أخبرت. وفي تلخيص الجامع للصدر : من الإنشاء ملك الإخبار كالوصي والمولى والمراجع والوكيل بالبيع ومن له الخيار. قال إذا حضت حيضة فأنت طالق فقال بعد مدة محتملة حضت وطهرت وقع، ولو قالت حضت وطهرت وأنا حائض لا حتى تطهر، ولو قال إذا حضت فقالت حضت منذ خمسة أيام وقع ولا تتهم في التأخير للعذر، ولو قالت وطهرت لا.
In al-Kafi: If she said after ten days 'I menstruated and became pure' and the husband denied her, she is divorced because she is trustworthy in her time. If she said after a month 'I menstruated and became pure, then menstruated another time, and now I am menstruating', her statement is not accepted, but when she becomes pure it occurs because she delayed the report from its time and became suspected. If he said 'if you menstruate, you are divorced' and she said after five days 'I menstruated and I am now menstruating', her word is accepted because the report is within its time. If she said 'I menstruated and became pure', she is not believed until she menstruates because she reported a situation contrary to the present. In Talkhis al-Jami' al-Sadr: Those with authority to create legal effects have the trust of reporting, like the executor, master, referent in divorce, agent for sale, and one with an option. He said: If he said 'when you menstruate a menstruation, you are divorced' and she said after a plausible period 'I menstruated and became pure', it occurs. If she said 'I menstruated and became pure and I am now menstruating', not until she becomes pure. If he said 'if you menstruate' and she said 'I menstruated five days ago', it occurs and she is not blamed for delay due to excuse. If she said 'and I became pure', no.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the wife's claim regarding her menstruation in the context of conditional divorce. The key principle is that the wife is considered trustworthy (amana) when reporting about her own menstruation, but only if she reports it in a timely manner (fi awaniha). If she delays, she becomes suspected (mutahama). For example, if she says after ten days that she menstruated and became pure, she is believed. But if she delays a month, her claim of current menstruation is not accepted until she actually becomes pure. Similarly, if the husband says 'if you menstruate' and she immediately says she is menstruating, her word is accepted. However, if she claims both menstruation and purity simultaneously, she is not believed until she actually menstruates. The passage also identifies who is considered trustworthy in such matters: those who have authority over the legal effect, like guardians and agents.

Key Terms
الأمانة (al-amānah): Trustworthiness; the wife is deemed trustworthy regarding her own menstruation when reporting in a timely manner.
الإخبار (al-ikhbār): Reporting a fact, here specifically about menstruation, which must be done within its proper time.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion; a wife who delays reporting becomes subject to suspicion and her word is not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'if you menstruate, you are divorced' and the wife says after five days 'I menstruated and am now menstruating', is she believed?
A) No, because she delayed.
B) Yes, because the report is within its time.
C) No, she must have witnesses.
D) Yes, but only if she is pure now.

Key Takeaway
For a wife's claim about menstruation to be accepted in conditional divorce, she must report it in a timely manner; delay makes her untrustworthy.

Conditional Divorce with Half of a Menstruation
Ruling when divorce is conditioned on halves of a menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce involving halves of a menstruation and explain why the divorces occur only after a complete menstruation and purity.

Core Idea
A half menstruation is not a legal entity; the condition is only met upon full completion.

This lesson examines a specific conditional divorce scenario where the husband splits the condition into two halves. Understanding this ruling highlights the Hanafi requirement for completeness in conditions (shurut). The key insight: until the full menstruation and purity occur, no legal effect arises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The husband states two conditions: 'if you menstruate half a menstruation' and 'if you menstruate the other half'. Note that each half is tied to a separate divorce pronouncement.
2
Determine when the condition is fulfilled
Hanafi law requires a complete menstruation (haydah) and purity (tahr) for the condition to be met. Half a menstruation is not a complete legal entity. Therefore, the condition is only satisfied when she has completed a full menstruation and then becomes pure.
This is based on the principle that the condition must be a reality (haqiqah).
3
Apply the ruling
Nothing occurs until she menstruates fully and becomes pure. Upon completion, both divorces take effect simultaneously, not separately at each half.
If she menstruated half, then became pure (which is impossible without completing the menstruation), the condition is still not met.
4
Understand the thamarah
The practical consequence: even though the husband intended two separate conditions, they are effectively merged into one event. If he intended only one divorce upon the whole, the conditional wording might be reinterpreted, but here the text assumes two divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الجوهرة: إذا حضت نصف حيضة فأنت طالق وإذا حضت نصفها الآخر فأنت طالق لا يقع شيء ما لم تحض وتطهر، فإذا حاضت وطهرت وقع تطليقتان.
In al-Jawharah: If you menstruate half a menstruation, you are divorced; and if you menstruate the other half, you are divorced – nothing occurs until she menstruates and becomes pure. Then when she menstruates and becomes pure, two divorces occur.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This is a clear ruling on a conditional divorce where the husband splits the condition into two halves of a single menstruation. The condition is that she is divorced upon each half. The key point: no divorce occurs until she completes a full menstruation and becomes pure (tahir). Once she menstruates fully and becomes pure, both divorces take effect simultaneously. This is because a 'half menstruation' is not a complete legal entity; the condition is not fulfilled until the full menstruation is complete.

Key Terms
نصف الحيضة (nisf al-haydah): Half a menstruation; not a complete legal entity for fulfilling the condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'If you menstruate half a menstruation, you are divorced; if you menstruate the other half, you are divorced.' When do the divorces occur?
A) Upon each half immediately.
B) Only after she completes a full menstruation and becomes pure.
C) Only after she menstruates twice.
D) They never occur because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A condition split into halves of a single menstruation is not fulfilled until the entire menstruation is complete and purity follows; both divorces occur simultaneously at that point.

Successive Conditional Divorce Oaths and Menstruation
Ruling on multiple conditional divorce oaths regarding menstruation counts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding successive conditional divorce oaths to determine when divorces occur based on the wording used (with or without 'thumma').

Core Idea
When multiple conditional divorce oaths share a condition, the first menstruation can count toward both oaths unless the word 'thumma' imposes a strict sequence.

This passage from al-Muhit illustrates a nuanced scenario in Hanafi fiqh: a husband makes two conditional divorce oaths about menstruation. The ruling depends on the conjunction used between the oaths. Understanding this helps you see how conditions can overlap and the importance of word choice in legal effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making successive conditional divorce oaths regarding menstruation. The ruling: divorces occur based on condition fulfillment.
Each oath is a separate conditional divorce.
2
Understand the condition sharing mechanism
Without 'thumma', the first menstruation fulfills the first oath fully and contributes half to the second (since the second requires two menstruations).
The first menstruation is 'every condition' for the first and 'half the condition' for the second.
3
Recognize the effect of the word 'thumma'
When 'thumma' is used, it implies succession with delay (tarakhi). The second condition must occur after the first is fully satisfied.
Thus, nothing occurs until two menstruations happen after the first.
4
Apply to scenarios
Given a scenario with or without 'thumma', determine the number of divorces that have occurred at each menstruation event.
Practice with examples: she menstruates once vs. twice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لو قال إذا حضت حيضة فأنت طالق ثم قال إن حضت حيضتين فأنت طالق فحاضت حيضة يقع واحدة باليمين الأول، فإذا حاضت أخرى يقع أخرى باليمين الثانية لأن الحيضة الأولى كل الشرط لليمين الأولى وشطر الشرط لليمين الثانية، فإذا حاضت أخرى فقد تم الشرط لليمين الثانية، فإن قال ثم إذا حاضت والمسألة بحالها لا يقع شيء حتى يوجد حيضتان بعد الأولى لأن كلمة «ثم» للتعقيب مع التراخي فيقتضي وجود الحيضتين بعد الأولى.
In al-Muhit: If he said 'if you menstruate a menstruation, you are divorced', then he said 'if you menstruate two menstruations, you are divorced', and she menstruated one menstruation, one divorce occurs by the first oath. When she menstruates another, another divorce occurs by the second oath, because the first menstruation is the entire condition for the first oath and half the condition for the second oath. When she menstruates another, the condition for the second oath is completed. If he said 'then if you menstruate' while the situation remains, nothing occurs until two menstruations occur after the first because the word 'thumma' indicates succession with delay, so it requires the existence of two menstruations after the first.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit explains the effect of successive conditional divorce oaths about menstruation. Example: husband says 'if you menstruate once, you are divorced' (first oath), then later says 'if you menstruate twice, you are divorced' (second oath). If she menstruates once, the first divorce occurs because the condition of the first oath is fulfilled. That same menstruation counts as half the condition for the second oath (since it requires two menstruations). When she menstruates a second time, the second divorce occurs because the condition of the second oath is now complete. However, if he uses the word 'thumma' (then) between the oaths, it implies that the second condition (two menstruations) must occur after the first condition is fully satisfied, so nothing occurs until two menstruations happen after the first one.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A conjunction meaning 'then' indicating succession with delay (tarakhi).
التعقيب (al-ta'qeeb): Successive order; in oaths, it affects how conditions combine.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): Delay; thumma implies a delay between conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'If you menstruate once, you are divorced. If you menstruate twice, you are divorced.' (without 'thumma'). She menstruates once. What happens?
A) Only one divorce occurs from the first oath.
B) Two divorces occur immediately.
C) Nothing occurs until she menstruates twice.
D) One divorce occurs, and when she menstruates a second time, another divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, repeated conditional divorce oaths can share a common condition; the first occurrence counts toward all conditions unless a sequential conjunction ('thumma') is used to delay later conditions.

Conditional Divorce with Twins: Judicial and Precautionary Rulings
Ruling on conditional divorce with twins, order unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the judicial (qada') and precautionary (tanzih) rulings for a conditional divorce based on gender when twins of both sexes are born and the order is unknown.

Core Idea
When uncertainty exists, the minimum number of divorces is applied judicially, but the maximum is recommended as a precaution.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with a complex scenario of conditional divorce. The husband conditions divorce on the gender of the child, and the wife gives birth to twins of both sexes with unknown birth order. The Hanafi jurists distinguish between what is certain (qada') and what is precautionary (tanzih). We will explore how they resolve the uncertainty and why the waiting period ends with the second birth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statement
The husband says: 'If you give birth to a male, you are divorced once; if you give birth to a female, you are divorced twice.' This creates two possible outcomes based on the gender of the firstborn.
2
List the possible scenarios
If the male is born first → one divorce occurs. If the female is born first → two divorces occur. Since the order is unknown, both are possible.
3
Apply the judicial certainty principle
Only one divorce is certain (the minimum), so the judge rules that one divorce has occurred (qada'an). The second divorce is doubtful and not enforced judicially.
This follows the legal maxim: 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.'
4
Apply the precautionary principle
To be on the safe side, the couple is advised to consider two divorces as a precaution (tanzihan), meaning the husband should treat it as two divorces in terms of remaining options.
This is not a binding judgment but a recommended caution.
5
Understand the waiting period (iddah)
The iddah ends with the birth of the second child. Therefore, no further divorce can occur through this condition, and the husband's right to return (raj'ah) expires.
Even if two divorces are precautionarily applied, the iddah has already ended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وفي إن ولدت ذكراً فأنت طالق واحدة وإن ولدت أنثى فثنتين فولدتهما ولم يدر الأول تطلق واحدة قضاء وثنتين تنزهاً ومضت العدة لأنها لو ولدت الغلام وقعت واحدة وتنقضي عدتها بوضع الجارية ثم لا يقع أخرى به لأنه حال انقضاء العدة، ولو ولدت الجارية أولاً وقعت تطليقتان وانقضت عدتها بوضع الغلام ثم لا يقع شيء آخر به لما ذكرنا أنه حال انقضاء العدة فإذا في حال تقع واحدة وفي حال تقع ثنتان فلا تقع الثانية بالشك والأولى أن يؤخذ بالثنتين تنزهاً واحتياطاً والعدة منقضية بيقين لما بينا قيد بقوله «لم يدر الأول» لأنه لو علم فقد بيناه وإن اختلفا فالقول للزوج لإنكاره . وأشار بمضي العدة إلى أنه لا رجعة ولا إرث كما في غاية البيان. وقيد بقوله إن ولدت لأنه لو قال إن كان حملك غلاماً فطالق واحدة أو جارية فثنتين فولدتهما لم تطلق لأن حملك اسم جنس مضاف فيعم كله فما لم يكن الكل غلاماً أو جارية لم يقع كما في قوله إن كان ما في بطنك غلاماً والباقي بحاله. وقوله إن كان ما في هذا العدل حنطة فهي طالق أو دقيقاً فطالق فإذا فيه حنطة ودقيق لا تطلق بخلاف قوله إن كان في بطنك غلام والباقي بحاله حيث تقع الثلاث. وقيد بقوله «فولدتهما» أي الغلام والجارية لأنها لو ولدت غلاماً وجاريتين ولم يدر الأول وقع الثلاث تنزهاً وثنتين قضاء، ولو ولدت غلامين وجارية وقعت واحدة قضاء وثلاث تنزهاً. وقدمنا أن الولادة لا تثبت بقولها اتفاقاً بل لا بد من نصاب الشهادة عنده وامرأة عندهم. ولو علق طلاقها بولادتها ولداً فولدت ميتاً طلقت وسيأتي تمامه في الأيمان وفي المحيط : قال كلما ولدت
His statement: (and if he says 'if you give birth to a male, you are divorced one, and if you give birth to a female, two', and she gave birth to both and the first is not known, she is divorced one judicially and two as a precaution, and the waiting period has passed). Because if she gave birth to the male first, one divorce occurs and her waiting period ends with the delivery of the female, and then no further divorce occurs because it is at the end of the waiting period. If she gave birth to the female first, two divorces occur and her waiting period ends with the delivery of the male, and then nothing else occurs because it is at the end of the waiting period. So in one scenario one divorce occurs, in another two, so the second divorce does not occur due to doubt, and it is better to take two as a precaution and precaution, and the waiting period is definitely concluded. The condition 'if he does not know the first' is mentioned because if he knows, it has been explained. If they differ, the husband's word is taken due to his denial. And the indication of the passage of the waiting period means no return and no inheritance as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And the condition 'if she gives birth' is mentioned because if he said 'if your pregnancy is a male, you are divorced one, or a female, two', and she gave birth to both, she is not divorced because 'your pregnancy' is a generic noun in construct and encompasses all, so unless all is male or female, it does not occur, as in his saying 'if what is in your womb is a male, etc.' And his saying 'if what is in this container is wheat, she is divorced, or flour, she is divorced' – if it contains both wheat and flour, she is not divorced, unlike his saying 'if there is a male in your womb, etc.' where three occur. And the condition 'she gave birth to both' means male and female, because if she gave birth to a male and two females and the first is unknown, three occur as a precaution and two judicially. If she gave birth to two males and one female, one occurs judicially and three as a precaution. And we have stated that birth is not established by her word unanimously, but witnesses are required according to him (Abu Hanifa) and one woman according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And if he suspended her divorce on her giving birth to a child and she gave birth to a stillborn, she is divorced, and its completion will come in oaths. In al-Muhit: He said 'whenever she gives birth'...
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This lengthy passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with a complex conditional divorce based on the gender of the child. The husband says: 'If you give birth to a male, you are divorced once; if you give birth to a female, you are divorced twice.' The wife gives birth to twins, one male and one female, and the order of birth is unknown. The ruling: judicially (qada'), one divorce is applied because that is the minimum that definitely occurred (if the male came first, one divorce; if the female came first, two divorces, but due to uncertainty, only one is certain). However, as a precaution (tanzihan), two divorces are recommended to be on the safe side. The waiting period (iddah) ends with the birth of the second child, so no further divorces can occur. The passage also discusses variations: if the condition is phrased differently (e.g., 'your pregnancy is male'), it encompasses all, so if both sexes are present, no divorce occurs. It also covers cases with multiple births of the same or different genders. The authority weight is from the commentary, and the ruling is consistent with the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qadā’): Judicial ruling; the minimum number of divorces that are certain to have occurred.
التنزيه (al-tanzīh): Precautionary measure; applying the maximum possible number of divorces out of caution, though not judicially enforced.
العدة (al-‘iddah): Waiting period after divorce; here it ends with the birth of the second child.
الرجعة (al-raj‘ah): Return; the husband's right to take back his wife during the iddah of a revocable divorce; here, after iddah passes, no return is possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'If you give birth to a male, you are divorced once; if you give birth to a female, you are divorced twice.' The wife gives birth to twins (one male, one female) and the order of birth is unknown. What is the judicial (qada') ruling?
A) No divorce occurs due to uncertainty.
B) One divorce is applied.
C) Two divorces are applied.
D) Three divorces are applied.

Key Takeaway
In conditional divorce with unknown gender order, the minimum certain divorce is judicially applied, but the maximum is precautionary.
