وشمل ما إذا ادعى الاستثناء وأنكرته فإن القول قوله وكذا في دعوى الشرط، ولو شهدوا أنه طلق أو خالع بلا استثناء أو شهدوا بأنه لم يستثن تقبل وهذا مما تقبل فيه البينة على النفي لأنه في المعنى أمر وجودي لأنه عبارة عن ضم الشفتين عقيب التكلم بالموجب، وإن قالوا أطلقوا ولم نسمع منه غير كلمة الخلع والزوج الاستثناء فالقول له لجواز أنه قاله ولم يسمعوه والشرط سماعه لإسماعهم على ما عرف في الجامع الصغير، وفي الصغرى إذا ذكر البدل في الخلع لا تسمع دعوى الاستثناء؛ كذا في البزازية. وفي الخانية : لو قال الزوج طلقتك أمس وقلت إن شاء الله ففي ظاهر الرواية يكون في طالق بائناً قوله : (كقوله يا طالق يا زانية فالاستثناء على الكل قال الرملي : هنا غلط ولعله بعد قوله فالاستثناء عليه وإن كان لا يجب به حد ولا يقع به طلاق فالاستثناء على الكل الخ ولم أجد هذا نسخ البحر التي عندي ولا في نسخ البزازية ولا بد منه .اهـ. قلت وكذلك قوله وكذا أنت طالق يا صبية صوابه ولو قال أنت الخ ويوضح الأمر عبارة التتارخانية ونصها وفي نوادر بشر بن الوليد عن أبي يوسف إذا قال لها أنت طالق يا زانية ثلاثاً إن شاء الله فالاستثناء على الآخر وهو القذف ويقع الطلاق، وكذلك إذا قال لها أنت طالق يا طالق إن شاء الله تعالى ولو قال أنت طالق يا خبيثة إن شاء الله فالاستثناء على الكل ولا يقع الطلاق كأنه قال يا فلانة . وذكر ثمة أصلاً فقال : المذكور فى اخر الكلام إذا كان يقع به طلاق أو يجب به حد فالاستثناء عليه نحو قوله يا زانية ويا طالق وإن كان لا يجب به حد ولا يقع به طلاق فالاستثناء على الكل وذلك نحو قوله يا خبيثة انتهت واعلم أنا كتبنا أوائل فصل الطلاق قبل الدخول عن شرح التلخيص ما ملخصه أن قوله يا زانية إن تخلل بين الشرط والجزاء أو بين الإيجاب والاستثناء لم يكن قذفاً في الأصح، وإن تقدم أو تأخر كان قذفاً. وعن أبي يوسف لا يعد المتخلل فاصلاً فيقع الطلاق للحال ويجب اللعان. وعن محمد يتعلق الطلاق ويجب اللعان. وجه ظاهر الرواية أن يا زانية وإن كان جزاء إلا أن المراد منه النفي دون التحقيق ولأنه نداء للإعلام فلا يفصل فيتعلق الطلاق فكذا القذف
إن شاء الله لا وكذا يصح الاستثناء، القول قول الزوج، وذكر في النوادر خلافاً بين أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ فقال على قول أبي يوسف يقبل قول الزوج، وعلى قول محمد لا يقبل قوله ويقع الطلاق وعليه الاعتماد والفتوى احتياطاً في أمر الفروج في زمن غلب على الناس الفساد انتهى.
And it includes the case where he claims the exception and she denies it: his word is accepted, and similarly in the claim of a condition. If witnesses testify that he divorced or khalaʿa without exception, or testify that he did not make an exception, their testimony is accepted. This is a case where evidence is accepted to prove a negative, because in meaning it is an existential matter, as it is an expression of bringing the two lips together after speaking the operative word. If they say: 'He pronounced the divorce and we did not hear anything besides the word of khulʿ from him,' and the husband [claims] the exception, his word is accepted because it is possible he said it and they did not hear it; the condition for it to be heard is that they hear it, as known from al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr. In al-Ṣughrā: if the exchange is mentioned in khulʿ, the claim of exception is not heard; likewise in al-Bazzāziyya. In al-Khāniyya: if the husband says 'I divorced you yesterday and I said "if Allah wills"', then in Ẓāhir al-Riwāya it is an irrevocable divorce. His statement: [like his saying 'O divorced one, O adulteress, the exception is upon the whole' — al-Ramlī said: here there is an error, and it should be after his saying 'the exception is upon it' etc. I did not find this in my copies of al-Baḥr nor in copies of al-Bazzāziyya, and it is necessary. End. I say: similarly his saying 'and likewise you are divorced O girl' is correctly 'if he said you are...' and the statement of al-Tātārkhāniyya clarifies it. Its text: in Nawādir of Bishr ibn al-Walīd from Abū Yūsuf... [then the same principle repeated]. And know that we wrote at the beginning of the chapter of divorce before consummation from Sharḥ al-Talkhīṣ a summary: that his saying 'O adulteress' if it intervenes between the condition and the result or between the positive statement and the exception, is not considered qadhf in the most correct view. If it comes before or after, it is qadhf. From Abū Yūsuf: the intervening word is not considered a separator, so the divorce occurs immediately and liʿān becomes obligatory. From Muḥammad: the divorce is suspended and liʿān becomes obligatory. The basis of Ẓāhir al-Riwāya is that 'O adulteress' even if it is a condition, the intent is to deny rather than confirm, and because it is a call for notification, it does not separate, so the divorce is suspended; similarly also qadhf. 'If Allah wills' does not [prevent] and similarly the exception is valid, the husband's word is accepted. And it is mentioned in al-Nawādir a dispute between Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad: according to Abū Yūsuf, the husband's word is accepted; according to Muḥammad, his word is not accepted and the divorce occurs. Upon this [Muḥammad's view] is reliance and fatwā as a precaution in matters of private parts in a time when corruption has prevailed among people. End.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage addresses the procedural question: when the husband claims he made an exception (istithnāʾ) after pronouncing divorce, is his claim accepted? The general rule is that his word is accepted (the qawl qawluhu principle) because he is claiming a legal possibility and the wife may be unaware. Evidence from the wife or witnesses that he did not make an exception is admissible, even though it proves a negative, because the act of making an exception is a physical act (bringing lips together). The text then cites a dispute in al-Nawādir between Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan al-Shaybānī: Abū Yūsuf holds that the husband's claim of istithnāʾ is accepted; Muḥammad holds that it is not accepted and the divorce falls immediately. The relied-upon position (muftā bihi) is Muḥammad's view, taken as a precaution in an age of corruption. This is an intra-Hanafī dispute where the later school prefers the view of Muḥammad over Abū Yūsuf and over the Ẓāhir al-Riwāya position, which normally would be the stronger authority. The commentary by al-Ramlī corrects a textual error in the copy.

Key Terms
القول قوله (al-qawl qawluhu): The principle that the husband's statement is accepted in claims regarding divorce, including istithnāʾ
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The established transmitted rulings from the six books of Imam Muhammad, forming the core of the Hanafi school
النوادر (al-Nawādir): Rare transmissions not part of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah; often contain dissenting opinions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (muftā bihi) in this passage, if a husband claims he said 'in shāʾ Allāh' after pronouncing divorce, what is the ruling?
A) His claim is accepted and no divorce occurs.
B) His claim is not accepted and the divorce occurs.
C) The matter is decided by witnesses only.
D) The divorce becomes void ab initio.

Key Takeaway
In the operative Hanafi position, the husband's claim of exception after divorce is rejected to prevent abuse—precaution overrides the general rule.

The Scope of Istithnāʾ: Valid Contracts and Particles
Explains scope of istithnāʾ and effects of particles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which contracts allow istithnāʾ and identify the effect of different particles (an, bi, li, fī) and attributions.

Core Idea
Istithnāʾ works in all declaratory utterances but the particle and the entity to whom the will is attributed determine whether the exception is effective.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq extends the discussion of istithnāʾ to contracts beyond ṭalāq. The author explains that 'in shāʾ Allāh' can be attached to sale, manumission, vows, and iʿtikāf, but not to commands and prohibitions. He then delves into the nuances of different particles and the attribution of will, showing how the choice of words and the entity to whom the will is ascribed can completely change the legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of valid contracts
Understand that istithnāʾ is valid in all ṣīgh al-akhbār (declaratory utterances) including performatives (inshāʾāt) like sale, iʿtikāf, manumission, and vows. Exclude commands and prohibitions.
2
Distinguish effective and ineffective attributions
If the will is attributed to Allah, the exception suspends occurrence. If attributed to beings whose will cannot be known (jinn, humans generally, angels, wall), the exception is ineffective. If attributed to a specific person (e.g., Zayd), it becomes a delegation (tamlīk) that requires that person's consent.
3
Analyze the particles and prepositions
The particle 'an' and its synonyms (illā, mā, idhā, bi) are valid for istithnāʾ. Prepositions 'bi' and 'li' have different effects: 'bi' with certain words like amr, ḥukm causes immediate effect; 'li' always causes immediate effect; 'fī' does not cause effect unless exceptionally close.
4
Resolve conflicts between sources
The passage notes that some later works (al-Bazzāziyya, al-Tātārkhāniyya) conflict with Ẓāhir al-Riwāya. The correct method is to follow Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, as it represents the madhhab.

Source Text

وأشار بصحة المشيئة في الطلاق إلى صحتها في كل ما كان من صيغ الأخبار وإن كانت انشاآت شرعاً فدخل البيع والاعتكاف والعتق والنذر بالصوم، وخرج الأمر والنهي . فلو قال اعتقوا عبدي في بعد موتي بع عبدي من بعد موتي إن شاء الله لا الاستثناء، وكذا بع عبدي هذا إن شاء الله لم يبعه . وخرج ما لم يختص باللسان كالنية فلو قال نويت أن أصوم إن شاء الله صح صومه. وأشار بإسناد المشيئة إلى الله تعالى إلى كل من لم يوقف له على مشيئة كإن شاء الجن أو الإنس أو الملائكة أو الحائط فلا يقع في الكل فخرج من يوقف له عليها كإن شاء زيد فهو تمليك له معتبر فيه مجلس علمه فإن شاء فيه طلقت وإلا خرج الأمر من يده وصورة مشيئته أن يقول شئت ما جعله إلى فلان ولا تشترط فيه نية الطلاق ولا ذكره كما في الجوهرة. ودخل في كلامه ما إذا علقه بمشيئة الله ومشيئة من يوقف على مشيئته كما إذا قال إن شاء الله وشاء زيد فلا وقوع وإن شاء زيد كما في البدائع. وقدمنا عن تلخيص الجامع حكم ما إذا قال أمرها بيد الله وبيدك . وأشار بكلمة «أن» إلى ما كان بمعناها فدخل إلا أن يشاء الله أو ما شاء الله أو إذا شاء الله أو بمشيئة الله وبالمشيئة إلى ما كان بمعناها كالإرادة والمحبة والرضا بجميع الأدوات المتقدمة لا فرق بين «إن» والباء فخرج ما لم يكن بمعناها كأمره وحكمه وإرادته وقضائه وإذنه وعلمه وقدرته فإنه يقع للحال إن كان بالباء، وإن أضافه إلى العبد وخرج أيضاً ما إذا كان باللام فإنه يقع في الوجوه كلها وإن أضافه إلى العبد، وأما إذا كان بـ«في وأضافه إلى الله تعالى فإنه لا يقع في الوجوه كلها إلا في بالأولى لقربه، فقد ظهر أن ما في البزازية والتتارخانية خلاف ظاهر الرواية، وعبارة متن التلخيص قدمها المؤلف أول باب التعليق. قوله: (وذكر في النوادر خلافاً إلى قوله انتهى) قال الرملي : هو بجملته منقول الخانية عن النوادر فقوله وعليه الاعتماد من كلام النوادر لا من كلام الخانية .اهـ وكتب قبله أقول : وحيثما وقع خلاف وترجيح لكل من القولين فالواجب الرجوع إلى ظاهر الرواية لأن ما عداها ليس مذهباً لأصحابنا . وأيضاً كما غلب الفساد في الرجال غلب في النساء فقد تكون كارهة له فتطلب الخلاص منه فتفتري عليه فيفتي المفتي بظاهر الرواية الذي هو المذهب ويفوض باطن الأمر إلى الله تعالى فتأمل. وأنصف من نفسك. قوله : (أو ما شاء الله قال في النهر : اعلم أن عدم الوقوع في ما شاء الله مسلم بتقدير كون ما مصدرية ظرفية لا ما إذا قدرت موصولاـولاً اسمياً أي الذي شاء الله تعالى من الواقع واحدة أو ثنتين أو ثلاثة ولا شك في أنت طالق المذكور هنا فصار كقوله أنت طالق كيف
And he indicated by the validity of [the exception with] the will in divorce its validity in all declaratory forms even if they are legally performative utterances, so includes sale, iʿtikāf, manumission, and the vow to fast, and excludes command and prohibition. So if he says 'Set free my slave after my death, sell my slave after my death, if Allah wills' — the exception is not [valid], and similarly if he says 'Sell this my slave, if Allah wills' — he does not sell him. And it excludes what is not specific to the tongue like intention, so if he says 'I intend to fast, if Allah wills' — his fast is valid. And he indicated by attributing the will to Allah the Exalted to everyone whose will one cannot be informed of — like 'if the jinn will' or 'people' or 'angels' or 'the wall' — then it does not occur in all [cases]; so it excludes one whose will one can be informed of — like 'if Zayd wills' — for this is a grant to him, and his knowledge is taken into consideration, if he wills in it, she is divorced, otherwise the matter leaves his hand. The form of his will is to say 'I will what I have made to so-and-so,' and intention of divorce nor its mention is not required, as in al-Jawhara. And included in his speech is when he suspends it on the will of Allah and the will of someone whose will can be informed of, like if he says 'if Allah wills and Zayd wills' — then no occurrence, even if Zayd wills, as in al-Badāʾiʿ. And we have earlier presented from Talkhīṣ al-Jāmiʿ the ruling of when he says 'her affair is in the hand of Allah and your hand.' And he indicated by the word 'an' to what is in its meaning, so it includes 'except if Allah wills' or 'what Allah wills' or 'when Allah wills' or 'by the will of Allah' and 'by the will' to what is in its meaning like desire, love, pleasure, with all the advanced tools; there is no difference between 'in' and the preposition 'bi'. So it excludes what is not in its meaning like His command, judgment, will, decree, permission, knowledge, power — then it takes effect immediately if it is with 'bi', and if he adds it to the slave, it also excludes when it is with 'li', for it takes effect in all aspects even if he adds it to the slave. As for when it is with 'fi' and he adds it to Allah the Exalted, then it does not take effect in all aspects except in the first due to its proximity. So it has become clear that what is in al-Bazzāziyya and al-Tātārkhāniyya is contrary to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, and the expression of the text of al-Talkhīṣ was presented by the author at the beginning of the chapter of taʿlīq. His statement: 'And it is mentioned in al-Nawādir a dispute...' al-Ramlī said: it is entirely transmitted from al-Khāniyya from al-Nawādir, so his statement 'upon this is reliance' is from the words of al-Nawādir, not from al-Khāniyya. End. And he wrote before it: I say: wherever a dispute occurs and there is tarjīḥ for each of the two statements, the duty is to return to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya because what is beyond it is not the madhhab of our companions. And also, just as corruption has prevailed among men, it has also prevailed among women, so she may be dislike him and seek deliverance from him and thus fabricate against him. So the muftī gives fatwā according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, which is the madhhab, and leaves the inner reality to Allah the Exalted. So reflect. And be fair to yourself. His statement: 'or what Allah wills' — in al-Nahr: know that non-occurrence in 'what Allah wills' (mā shāʾ Allāh) is accepted on the assumption that 'mā' is a verbal noun in the sense of time, not when it is understood as a relative pronoun meaning 'that which Allah wills' from the actual occurrence — one, two, or three times — and there is no doubt that 'you are divorced' mentioned here becomes like his saying 'you are divorced how'.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage extends the discussion of istithnāʾ beyond ṭalāq to other contracts and performs. The author explains that the validity of attaching 'in shāʾ Allāh' is not limited to divorce; it applies to all declaratory utterances (akhbār) even if they are legally performative (inshāʾāt) like sale, iʿtikāf, manumission, and vows. However, it does not apply to commands and prohibitions (like 'sell' or 'set free') because those are immediate orders. The exception also works with intention (niyya) outside direct speech. The passage then discusses the attribution of will: if it is attributed to beings whose will one cannot know (jinn, humans, angels, even a wall), the exception is ineffective and the divorce does not occur? Actually, it says 'fala yaqaʿ fī al-kull' meaning it does not occur in any case? The text is a bit ambiguous but likely means the taʿlīq is invalid. If attributed to someone like Zayd whose will can be known, it becomes a delegation (tamlīk) and Zayd's choice matters. The author then discusses different particles used for exception: 'an' and its synonyms (illā an yashāʾ Allāh, mā shāʾ Allāh, idhā shāʾ Allāh, bi-mashīʾat Allāh) are valid. The prepositions 'in' and 'bi' are the same in effect. However, words like 'amr', 'ḥukm', 'irāda', etc., if used with 'bi', cause immediate effect unless added to the slave. The letter 'li' always causes immediate effect. The letter 'fī' does not cause effect unless exceptionally close. Finally, the author notes that the rulings in al-Bazzāziyya and al-Tātārkhāniyya conflict with Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, and the proper method is to follow Ẓāhir al-Riwāya in case of dispute. A comment on 'mā shāʾ Allāh' clarifies that if it means 'whatever Allah wills' (relative pronoun), then the divorce occurs as intended by Allah; the non-occurrence is only if it means 'if Allah wills at that time'. This is a complex but essential passage for understanding the Hanafi technicalities of taʿlīq.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashīʾah): Will; the attribute of Allah referred to in 'in shāʾ Allāh'
صيغ الأخبار (ṣīgh al-akhbār): Declaratory formulas that are legally effective, including those that are inshāʾ (performative)
تمليك (tamlīk): Making something the property of another; here, delegating the choice of divorce to another person
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāya): The authoritative transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a husband says 'You are divorced bi-irādat Allāh' (by the will of Allah)?
A) Divorce occurs immediately because irāda is not in the meaning of mashīʾa.
B) Divorce is suspended because irāda is among the synonyms of mashīʾa.
C) The divorce is invalid because irāda is not a valid expression.
D) The ruling depends on the wife's intention.

Key Takeaway
Istithnāʾ is valid in all declaratory contracts, but the specific particle and the entity to whom the will is attributed determine whether the exception is effective; always refer to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya in case of conflict.

Talaq — Divorce

Exception with 'In Sha Allah' in Divorce: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the ruling on exception with 'In Sha Allah' in divorce and the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on istithna in divorce and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, identifying the mufta bihi and its rationale.

Core Idea
In divorce, the husband's claim of exception is accepted in principle, but the mufta bihi rejects it as a precaution in corrupt times.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the core ruling on exception (istithna) with 'In Sha Allah' in divorce, then immediately introduces an intra-Hanafi disagreement recorded in al-Nawadir. The basic ruling is that the exception is valid and the divorce does not occur if the husband so claims. However, a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani leads to a different operative ruling for fatwa. Understanding this dispute reveals how later Hanafi authorities prioritized precaution (ihtiyat) over the general principle of accepting a party's word, especially in an age of moral decay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'إن شاء الله لا يقع الطلاق، وكذا يصح الاستثناء، القول قول الزوج'. What is the default ruling regarding a husband who says 'In Sha Allah' after pronouncing divorce?
The default ruling is that the divorce does not occur and the husband's word is accepted (his claim of exception is believed).
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
The phrase 'وذكر في النوادر خلافاً بين أبي يوسف ومحمد' signals that a different transmission exists. Identify the two positions: what does Abu Yusuf hold? What does Muhammad hold?
Abu Yusuf: accept the husband's word (divorce does not occur). Muhammad: do not accept his word (divorce occurs).
3
Understand the reasoning behind each position
Though the passage does not give explicit proofs, infer the underlying principles. Abu Yusuf relies on the general rule that the word of the person making a claim is taken (al-qaul qauluhu). Muhammad relies on precaution in marriage (ihtiyat fi umur al-furuj) and the prevalence of corruption.
The rationale is based on social context: in an age of corruption, people might falsely claim exception to avoid divorce.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Compare the two scenarios: under Abu Yusuf's view, if the husband claims the exception, the divorce never occurs; under Muhammad's view, the divorce takes effect despite his claim.
The practical difference is whether the marriage continues or ends.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its rationale
The passage explicitly states: 'وعليه الاعتماد والفتوى احتياطاً في أمر الفروج في زمن غلب على الناس الفساد'. What is the relied-upon position and why?
Muhammad's view is mufta bihi, out of precaution in marriage matters in corrupt times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن شاء الله لا يقع الطلاق، وكذا يصح الاستثناء، القول قول الزوج، وذكر في النوادر خلافاً بين أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ فقال على قول أبي يوسف يقبل قول الزوج، وعلى قول محمد لا يقبل قوله ويقع الطلاق وعليه الاعتماد والفتوى احتياطاً في أمر الفروج في زمن غلب على الناس الفساد انتهى.
If Allah wills, the divorce does not occur, and similarly the exception is valid. The husband's word is accepted. And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir that there is a difference of opinion between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: according to Abu Yusuf's view, the husband's statement is accepted; according to Muhammad's view, his statement is not accepted and the divorce occurs. And upon his view is reliance and fatwa as a precaution in matters of marriage in an age when corruption among people has become prevalent. End.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling regarding the exception (istithna') with 'In Sha Allah' in divorce. The basic ruling is that if a husband says 'You are divorced, if Allah wills,' the divorce does not take effect. The husband's claim that he intended the exception is accepted (القول قول الزوج). However, in the Nawadir (rare transmissions) a disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is recorded. Abu Yusuf accepts the husband's claim, while Muhammad does not and rules that the divorce occurs. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Muhammad's view, out of precaution in matters of marriage, especially in corrupt times. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): Making an exception by saying 'إلا' or 'إن شاء الله' etc. to exclude the effect of a pronouncement.
النوادر (al-nawādir): Rare or less authentic transmissions from the Hanafi imams, as opposed to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this passage, if a husband says 'You are divorced if Allah wills' and claims he intended the exception, what is the ruling?
A) The husband's word is accepted and the divorce does not occur.
B) The husband's word is not accepted and the divorce occurs.
C) The divorce occurs regardless of his claim.
D) The exception is invalid.

Key Takeaway
For fatwa, the mufta bihi in this matter is Muhammad's view—the husband's claim of exception with 'In Sha Allah' is not accepted, and the divorce takes effect, as a precaution against corruption.

Exception with 'In Sha Allah' Beyond Divorce: Valid in Declarative Sentences
Expansion of exception ruling to various statements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of statements (declarative vs. imperative) are affected by the exception 'In Sha Allah' and apply the ruling on attributing the will to known vs. unknown entities.

Core Idea
The exception 'In Sha Allah' prevents occurrence only in news-like statements, not commands or prohibitions.

The Hanafi school extends the ruling on exception from divorce to other declarative acts like sale and manumission. This lesson clarifies which statements are included and how attributing the will to different entities changes the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement type
Determine whether the utterance is declarative (khabar) or imperative (insha'). The exception only affects declarative statements.
Commands and prohibitions are excluded immediately.
2
Check the attribution of the will
If the exception is attributed to someone whose will is known (like a named person), it becomes a delegation (tamlik) requiring his consent. If attributed to an unknown entity (jinn, angels, wall), the exception has no effect.
This distinction applies regardless of the statement type.
3
Apply the ruling
For declarative statements with the exception attributed to Allah, the act does not occur. For imperative statements, the exception is invalid and the command stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ما إذا كان باللام فإنه يقع في الوجوه كلها وإن أضافه إلى العبد، وأما إذا كان بـ«في وأضافه إلى الله تعالى فإنه لا يقع في الوجوه كلها إلا في بالاولى لقربه، فقد ظهر أن ما في البزازية والتتارخانية خلاف ظاهر الرواية، وعبارة متن التلخيص قدمها المؤلف أول باب التعليق. قوله: (وذكر في النوادر خلافاً إلى قوله انتهى) قال الرملي : هو بجملته منقول الخانية عن النوادر فقوله وعليه الاعتماد من كلام النوادر لا من كلام الخانية .اهـ وكتب قبله أقول : وحيثما وقع خلاف وترجيح لكل من القولين فالواجب الرجوع إلى ظاهر الرواية لأن ما عداها ليس مذهباً لأصحابنا . وأيضاً كما غلب الفساد في الرجال غلب في النساء فقد تكون كارهة مسلم بتقدير كون ما مصدرية ظرفية لا ما إذا قدرت موصولا ـولاً اسمياً أي الذي شاء الله تعالى من الواقع واحدة أو ثنتين أو ثلاثة ولا شك في أنت طالق المذكور هنا فصار كقوله أنت طالق كيف قوله طالق في علم الله، وإلا في قوله في قدرة الله إن أراد بالقدرة ضد العجز لأن قدرة الله تعالى موجودة قطعاً كالعلم سواء بخلاف ما إذا لم ينو لأنها بمعنى التقدير ولا يعلم تقديره؛ كذا في المحيط . والحاصل أنه إن أتى بـ «إن لم يقع في الكل، وإن أتى بالباء لم يقع في المشيئة والإرادة والرضا والمحبة ووقع في الباقي، وإن أتى بـ«في» لم يقع إلا في علم الله، وإن أتى باللام وقع في الكل، وإن أضافه إلى العبد كان تمليكاً في الأربعة الأولى وهي المشيئة وأخواتها وما بمعناها كالهوية والرؤية تعليقاً في الستة وهي الأمر وأخواته .
And he indicated, by the validity of the will (mashi'ah) in divorce, its validity in everything that is from the forms of declarative sentences, even if they are legally constructive, so included are sale, i'tikaf, manumission, and vow of fasting, and excluded are command and prohibition. So if he says 'Free my slave after my death' or 'Sell my slave after my death' with 'if Allah wills', the exception [is valid] and he does not sell. And likewise 'Sell this slave of mine' with 'if Allah wills', he does not sell him. And excluded is what is not specific to the tongue, like intention, so if he says 'I intend to fast if Allah wills', his fast is valid. And he indicated, by attributing the will to Allah Almighty, that for everyone whose will is not known, like 'if the jinn will' or 'if humans will' or 'if angels will' or 'if the wall wills', [the exception] does not occur in all. So excluded is the one whose will is known, like 'if Zaid wills', so it is a delegation (tamlik) for him conditional upon his knowledge of the council; if he wills in it, she is divorced, otherwise the matter leaves his hand. And the form of his willing is that he says 'I will what I have given to so-and-so', and intention of divorce is not required nor its mention, as in al-Jawharah. And included in his speech is when he suspends it upon Allah's will and the will of one whose will is known, such as if he says 'If Allah wills and Zaid wills', then there is no occurrence unless Zaid wills, as in al-Bada'i'. And we have previously given from Talkhis al-Jami' the ruling when he says 'Her affair is in the hand of Allah and in your hand.' And he indicated by the word 'an' (that) to what is in its meaning, so included are 'unless Allah wills' or 'what Allah wills' or 'when Allah wills' or 'by Allah's will', and by 'will' to what is in its meaning like desire (iradah), love (mahabbah), and pleasure (rida) with all the aforementioned tools; there is no difference between 'in' and 'ba'. So excluded is what is not in its meaning, like His command, His judgment, His decree, His permission, His knowledge, and His power; for it occurs immediately if with 'ba', and if he attributes it to the servant. And also excluded is when it is with 'lam', for it occurs in all cases even if he attributes it to the servant. As for when it is with 'fi' and attributing it to Allah Almighty, it does not occur in all cases except in the first because of its proximity. Thus it appears that what is in al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Tatar Khaniyyah contradicts the apparent transmission, and the wording of the text of al-Talkhis was presented by the author at the beginning of the chapter on suspension. [Commentary:] His saying: (And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir there is a difference until his saying 'end') al-Ramli said: It is entirely transmitted from al-Khaniyyah from al-Nawadir; his saying 'upon it is reliance' is from the words of al-Nawadir, not from al-Khaniyyah. End. And before it he wrote: I say: Whenever there is a difference and a preference for each of the two views, the obligation is to refer to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), for what is other than it is not the madhhab of our companions. Also, just as corruption has prevailed among men, it has prevailed among women; she may be averse to him and seek release from him, so she may slander him. So the mufti gives fatwa according to the apparent transmission, which is the madhhab, and he entrusts the inner reality to Allah Almighty, so reflect. And be fair to yourself. His saying: (or what Allah wills) He said in al-Nahr: Know that non-occurrence in 'ma sha Allah' is accepted on the assumption that 'ma' is a verbal noun indicating time, not if it is taken as a relative pronoun, i.e., that which Allah willed from reality, one, two, or three, and there is no doubt that 'you are divorced' mentioned here becomes like his saying 'you are divorced how'. His saying: 'divorced in the knowledge of Allah' except in his saying 'in the power of Allah' if he intended by power the opposite of impotence, for the power of Allah Almighty certainly exists like knowledge, unlike if he did not intend because it means predestination and its predestination is not known. So in al-Muhit. The conclusion: if he uses 'in' it does not occur in all; if he uses 'ba' it does not occur in the will (mashi'ah), desire (iradah), pleasure (rida), love (mahabbah), and occurs in the rest; if he uses 'fi' it does not occur except in the knowledge of Allah; if he uses 'lam' it occurs in all; and if he attributes it to the servant, it becomes a delegation (tamlik) in the first four, namely will and its sisters and what is in their meaning like inclination (hawa) and vision (ru'ya), and a suspension (ta'liq) in the six, namely command and its sisters.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This lengthy passage expands the ruling on the exception with 'In Sha Allah' to various other statements and contexts. It begins by affirming that the exception is valid not only in divorce but in all declarative sentences (akhbar), even if they are legally constructive (insha'at) such as sale, manumission, and vows. Commands and prohibitions are excluded. It then discusses the effect of attributing the exception to someone whose will is known or unknown. If the will is unknown (e.g., jinn, angels, wall), the exception does not occur. If known (e.g., Zaid), it becomes a delegation (tamlik) requiring his consent. The passage then examines different particles (إن, ب, ل, ف, في) and words (mashi'ah, iradah, mahabbah, rida, amr, hukm, etc.) and their impact. The summary: with 'إن' the divorce never occurs; with 'ب' it does not occur with words meaning 'will' but occurs with other words like 'knowledge' etc.; with 'في' it only occurs with 'knowledge of Allah'; with 'لام' it occurs in all cases. When attributed to a servant, the first four words (mashi'ah etc.) become tamlik, and the last six (amr etc.) remain ta'liq. The passage also includes a commentary clarifying that the relied-upon position for such disputes is the Zahir al-Riwayah, as the Nawadir are not the madhhab. The discussion on 'ما شاء الله' and 'في علم الله' clarifies that non-occurrence depends on proper interpretation. This passage is a comprehensive guide to the nuances of istithna' in divorce and other acts.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashi'ah): Will of Allah or a person; when used in exception, it prevents the occurrence of the act.
تمليك (tamlik): Delegation of the right to divorce to another person, conditional on his consent within the council.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man says 'I divorce you if the wall wills', what is the ruling?
A) The divorce occurs immediately.
B) The divorce does not occur because the wall's will is unknown.
C) The divorce is suspended until the wall wills.
D) The statement is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The exception 'In Sha Allah' prevents occurrence only in news-like statements, and attributing the will to unknown entities renders the exception ineffective.

Talaq — Divorce

Particles and Words in Ta'liq: A Grid of Rulings
Systematic breakdown of particle and word effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for different particles (in, bi, lam, fi) and words (mashi'ah, iradah, etc.) to determine whether a divorce occurs immediately, not at all, or is suspended.

Core Idea
The ruling changes based on the particle and word used; a systematic grid guides the mufti.

The passage provides a detailed grid of rulings based on the particle (إن, ب, ل, ف) and the word used (mashi'ah, iradah, etc.). This lesson helps you navigate that grid to accurately determine the legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle
Determine which particle is used: إن (in), ب (bi), ل (lam), ف (fi). Each has a distinct effect.
In this passage, 'إن' and 'ب' are considered the same for mashi'ah but differ for other words.
2
Identify the word
Classify the word as belonging to one of two groups: (1) mashi'ah and its sisters (iradah, mahabbah, rida) or (2) amr and its sisters (hukm, qada', idhn, 'ilm, qudrah, etc.).
3
Apply the grid
Use the grid: With 'إن', divorce never occurs. With 'ب', it does not occur for mashi'ah group, but occurs for amr group. With 'في', it only occurs for 'ilm Allah. With 'لام', it occurs in all cases.
4
Consider attribution to a servant
If the word is attributed to a servant (e.g., 'if Zaid wills'), the first four words (mashi'ah group) become tamlik, and the last six (amr group) remain ta'liq (suspension).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بصحة المشيئة في الطلاق إلى صحتها في كل ما كان من صيغ الأخبار وإن كانت انشاآت شرعاً فدخل البيع والاعتكاف والعتق والنذر بالصوم، وخرج الأمر والنهي . فلو قال اعتقوا عبدي في بعد موتي بع عبدي من بعد موتي إن شاء الله لا الاستثناء، وكذا بع عبدي هذا إن شاء الله لم يبعه . وخرج ما لم يختص باللسان كالنية فلو قال نويت أن أصوم إن شاء الله صح صومه. وأشار بإسناد المشيئة إلى الله تعالى إلى كل من لم يوقف له على مشيئة كإن شاء الجن أو الإنس أو الملائكة أو الحائط فلا يقع في الكل فخرج من يوقف له عليها كإن شاء زيد فهو تمليك له معتبر فيه مجلس علمه فإن شاء فيه طلقت وإلا خرج الأمر من يده وصورة مشيئته أن يقول شئت ما جعله إلى فلان ولا تشترط فيه نية الطلاق ولا ذكره كما في الجوهرة. ودخل في كلامه ما إذا علقه بمشيئة الله ومشيئة من يوقف على مشيئته كما إذا قال إن شاء الله وشاء زيد فلا وقوع وإن شاء زيد كما في البدائع. وقدمنا عن تلخيص الجامع حكم ما إذا قال أمرها بيد الله وبيدك . وأشار بكلمة «أن» إلى ما كان بمعناها فدخل إلا أن يشاء الله أو ما شاء الله أو إذا شاء الله أو بمشيئة الله وبالمشيئة إلى ما كان بمعناها كالإرادة والمحبة والرضا بجميع الأدوات المتقدمة لا فرق بين «إن» والباء فخرج ما لم يكن بمعناها كأمره وحكمه وإرادته وقضائه وإذنه وعلمه وقدرته فإنه يقع للحال إن كان بالباء، وإن أضافه إلى العبد وخرج أيضاً ما إذا كان باللام فإنه يقع في الوجوه كلها وإن أضافه إلى العبد، وأما إذا كان بـ«في وأضافه إلى الله تعالى فإنه لا يقع في الوجوه كلها إلا في بالاولى لقربه، فقد ظهر أن ما في البزازية والتتارخانية خلاف ظاهر الرواية، وعبارة متن التلخيص قدمها المؤلف أول باب التعليق. قوله: (وذكر في النوادر خلافاً إلى قوله انتهى) قال الرملي : هو بجملته منقول الخانية عن النوادر فقوله وعليه الاعتماد من كلام النوادر لا من كلام الخانية .اهـ وكتب قبله أقول : وحيثما وقع خلاف وترجيح لكل من القولين فالواجب الرجوع إلى ظاهر الرواية لأن ما عداها ليس مذهباً لأصحابنا . وأيضاً كما غلب الفساد في الرجال غلب في النساء فقد تكون كارهة له فتطلب الخلاص منه فتفتري عليه فيفتي المفتي بظاهر الرواية الذي هو المذهب ويفوض باطن الأمر إلى الله تعالى فتأمل. وأنصف من نفسك. قوله : (أو ما شاء الله قال في النهر : اعلم أن عدم الوقوع في ما شاء الله مسلم بتقدير كون ما مصدرية ظرفية لا ما إذا قدرت موصولا ـولاً اسمياً أي الذي شاء الله تعالى من الواقع واحدة أو ثنتين أو ثلاثة ولا شك في أنت طالق المذكور هنا فصار كقوله أنت طالق كيف قوله طالق في علم الله، وإلا في قوله في قدرة الله إن أراد بالقدرة ضد العجز لأن قدرة الله تعالى موجودة قطعاً كالعلم سواء بخلاف ما إذا لم ينو لأنها بمعنى التقدير ولا يعلم تقديره؛ كذا في المحيط . والحاصل أنه إن أتى بـ «إن لم يقع في الكل، وإن أتى بالباء لم يقع في المشيئة والإرادة والرضا والمحبة ووقع في الباقي، وإن أتى بـ«في» لم يقع إلا في علم الله، وإن أتى باللام وقع في الكل، وإن أضافه إلى العبد كان تمليكاً في الأربعة الأولى وهي المشيئة وأخواتها وما بمعناها كالهوية والرؤية تعليقاً في الستة وهي الأمر وأخواته .
And he indicated, by the validity of the will (mashi'ah) in divorce, its validity in everything that is from the forms of declarative sentences, even if they are legally constructive, so included are sale, i'tikaf, manumission, and vow of fasting, and excluded are command and prohibition. So if he says 'Free my slave after my death' or 'Sell my slave after my death' with 'if Allah wills', the exception [is valid] and he does not sell. And likewise 'Sell this slave of mine' with 'if Allah wills', he does not sell him. And excluded is what is not specific to the tongue, like intention, so if he says 'I intend to fast if Allah wills', his fast is valid. And he indicated, by attributing the will to Allah Almighty, that for everyone whose will is not known, like 'if the jinn will' or 'if humans will' or 'if angels will' or 'if the wall wills', [the exception] does not occur in all. So excluded is the one whose will is known, like 'if Zaid wills', so it is a delegation (tamlik) for him conditional upon his knowledge of the council; if he wills in it, she is divorced, otherwise the matter leaves his hand. And the form of his willing is that he says 'I will what I have given to so-and-so', and intention of divorce is not required nor its mention, as in al-Jawharah. And included in his speech is when he suspends it upon Allah's will and the will of one whose will is known, such as if he says 'If Allah wills and Zaid wills', then there is no occurrence unless Zaid wills, as in al-Bada'i'. And we have previously given from Talkhis al-Jami' the ruling when he says 'Her affair is in the hand of Allah and in your hand.' And he indicated by the word 'an' (that) to what is in its meaning, so included are 'unless Allah wills' or 'what Allah wills' or 'when Allah wills' or 'by Allah's will', and by 'will' to what is in its meaning like desire (iradah), love (mahabbah), and pleasure (rida) with all the aforementioned tools; there is no difference between 'in' and 'ba'. So excluded is what is not in its meaning, like His command, His judgment, His decree, His permission, His knowledge, and His power; for it occurs immediately if with 'ba', and if he attributes it to the servant. And also excluded is when it is with 'lam', for it occurs in all cases even if he attributes it to the servant. As for when it is with 'fi' and attributing it to Allah Almighty, it does not occur in all cases except in the first because of its proximity. Thus it appears that what is in al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Tatar Khaniyyah contradicts the apparent transmission, and the wording of the text of al-Talkhis was presented by the author at the beginning of the chapter on suspension. [Commentary:] His saying: (And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir there is a difference until his saying 'end') al-Ramli said: It is entirely transmitted from al-Khaniyyah from al-Nawadir; his saying 'upon it is reliance' is from the words of al-Nawadir, not from al-Khaniyyah. End. And before it he wrote: I say: Whenever there is a difference and a preference for each of the two views, the obligation is to refer to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), for what is other than it is not the madhhab of our companions. Also, just as corruption has prevailed among men, it has prevailed among women; she may be averse to him and seek release from him, so she may slander him. So the mufti gives fatwa according to the apparent transmission, which is the madhhab, and he entrusts the inner reality to Allah Almighty, so reflect. And be fair to yourself. His saying: (or what Allah wills) He said in al-Nahr: Know that non-occurrence in 'ma sha Allah' is accepted on the assumption that 'ma' is a verbal noun indicating time, not if it is taken as a relative pronoun, i.e., that which Allah willed from reality, one, two, or three, and there is no doubt that 'you are divorced' mentioned here becomes like his saying 'you are divorced how'. His saying: 'divorced in the knowledge of Allah' except in his saying 'in the power of Allah' if he intended by power the opposite of impotence, for the power of Allah Almighty certainly exists like knowledge, unlike if he did not intend because it means predestination and its predestination is not known. So in al-Muhit. The conclusion: if he uses 'in' it does not occur in all; if he uses 'ba' it does not occur in the will (mashi'ah), desire (iradah), pleasure (rida), love (mahabbah), and occurs in the rest; if he uses 'fi' it does not occur except in the knowledge of Allah; if he uses 'lam' it occurs in all; and if he attributes it to the servant, it becomes a delegation (tamlik) in the first four, namely will and its sisters and what is in their meaning like inclination (hawa) and vision (ru'ya), and a suspension (ta'liq) in the six, namely command and its sisters.

Commentary
This lengthy passage expands the ruling on the exception with 'In Sha Allah' to various other statements and contexts. Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of the divorce on a condition; if the condition occurs, the divorce takes effect.
تمليك (tamlik): Delegation of the right to divorce to another person, conditional on his consent within the council.

Relying on Zahir al-Riwayah in Contradictory Transmissions
Commentary on hierarchy of transmissions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and other layers of transmission and explain why the mufti must follow the apparent transmission in case of dispute.

Core Idea
When transmissions conflict, the mufti relies on the Zahir al-Riwayah; Nawadir are not the madhhab.

The commentary in this passage emphasizes a key principle: the relied-upon position is the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah). This lesson explains why other sources like Nawadir should not override it, and how this principle safeguards fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradiction
Note that the author points out a contradiction between what is found in al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Tatar Khaniyyah and the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah).
The apparent transmission is from the core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Apply the rule of tarjih
When there is a dispute and a preference is stated for each view, the obligation is to refer to the Zahir al-Riwayah because anything else is not the madhhab of the companions (i.e., the Hanafi school).
3
Consider the practical wisdom
The passage adds that due to potential corruption, the mufti must give fatwa according to the apparent transmission and entrust the inner reality to Allah.

الأولى وهي المشيئة وأخواتها وما بمعناها كالهوية والرؤية تعليقاً في الستة وهي الأمر وأخواته .
And he indicated, by the validity of the will (mashi'ah) in divorce, its validity in everything that is from the forms of declarative sentences, even if they are legally constructive, so included are sale, i'tikaf, manumission, and vow of fasting, and excluded are command and prohibition. So if he says 'Free my slave after my death' or 'Sell my slave after my death' with 'if Allah wills', the exception [is valid] and he does not sell. And likewise 'Sell this slave of mine' with 'if Allah wills', he does not sell him. And excluded is what is not specific to the tongue, like intention, so if he says 'I intend to fast if Allah wills', his fast is valid. And he indicated, by attributing the will to Allah Almighty, that for everyone whose will is not known, like 'if the jinn will' or 'if humans will' or 'if angels will' or 'if the wall wills', [the exception] does not occur in all. So excluded is the one whose will is known, like 'if Zaid wills', so it is a delegation (tamlik) for him conditional upon his knowledge of the council; if he wills in it, she is divorced, otherwise the matter leaves his hand. And the form of his willing is that he says 'I will what I have given to so-and-so', and intention of divorce is not required nor its mention, as in al-Jawharah. And included in his speech is when he suspends it upon Allah's will and the will of one whose will is known, such as if he says 'If Allah wills and Zaid wills', then there is no occurrence unless Zaid wills, as in al-Bada'i'. And we have previously given from Talkhis al-Jami' the ruling when he says 'Her affair is in the hand of Allah and in your hand.' And he indicated by the word 'an' (that) to what is in its meaning, so included are 'unless Allah wills' or 'what Allah wills' or 'when Allah wills' or 'by Allah's will', and by 'will' to what is in its meaning like desire (iradah), love (mahabbah), and pleasure (rida) with all the aforementioned tools; there is no difference between 'in' and 'ba'. So excluded is what is not in its meaning, like His command, His judgment, His decree, His permission, His knowledge, and His power; for it occurs immediately if with 'ba', and if he attributes it to the servant. And also excluded is when it is with 'lam', for it occurs in all cases even if he attributes it to the servant. As for when it is with 'fi' and attributing it to Allah Almighty, it does not occur in all cases except in the first because of its proximity. Thus it appears that what is in al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Tatar Khaniyyah contradicts the apparent transmission, and the wording of the text of al-Talkhis was presented by the author at the beginning of the chapter on suspension. [Commentary:] His saying: (And it is mentioned in al-Nawadir there is a difference until his saying 'end') al-Ramli said: It is entirely transmitted from al-Khaniyyah from al-Nawadir; his saying 'upon it is reliance' is from the words of al-Nawadir, not from al-Khaniyyah. End. And before it he wrote: I say: Whenever there is a difference and a preference for each of the two views, the obligation is to refer to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), for what is other than it is not the madhhab of our companions. Also, just as corruption has prevailed among men, it has prevailed among women; she may be averse to him and seek release from him, so she may slander him. So the mufti gives fatwa according to the apparent transmission, which is the madhhab, and he entrusts the inner reality to Allah Almighty, so reflect. And be fair to yourself. His saying: (or what Allah wills) He said in al-Nahr: Know that non-occurrence in 'ma sha Allah' is accepted on the assumption that 'ma' is a verbal noun indicating time, not if it is taken as a relative pronoun, i.e., that which Allah willed from reality, one, two, or three, and there is no doubt that 'you are divorced' mentioned here becomes like his saying 'you are divorced how'. His saying: 'divorced in the knowledge of Allah' except in his saying 'in the power of Allah' if he intended by power the opposite of impotence, for the power of Allah Almighty certainly exists like knowledge, unlike if he did not intend because it means predestination and its predestination is not known. So in al-Muhit. The conclusion: if he uses 'in' it does not occur in all; if he uses 'ba' it does not occur in the will (mashi'ah), desire (iradah), pleasure (rida), love (mahabbah), and occurs in the rest; if he uses 'fi' it does not occur except in the knowledge of Allah; if he uses 'lam' it occurs in all; and if he attributes it to the servant, it becomes a delegation (tamlik) in the first four, namely will and its sisters and what is in their meaning like inclination (hawa) and vision (ru'ya), and a suspension (ta'liq) in the six, namely command and its sisters.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This lengthy passage expands the ruling on the exception with 'In Sha Allah' to various other statements and contexts. It begins by affirming that the exception is valid not only in divorce but in all declarative sentences (akhbar), even if they are legally constructive (insha'at) such as sale, manumission, and vows. Commands and prohibitions are excluded. It then discusses the effect of attributing the exception to someone whose will is known or unknown. If the will is unknown (e.g., jinn, angels, wall), the exception does not occur. If known (e.g., Zaid), it becomes a delegation (tamlik) requiring his consent. The passage then examines different particles (إن, ب, ل, ف, في) and words (mashi'ah, iradah, mahabbah, rida, amr, hukm, etc.) and their impact. The summary: with 'إن' the divorce never occurs; with 'ب' it does not occur with words meaning 'will' but occurs with other words like 'knowledge' etc.; with 'في' it only occurs with 'knowledge of Allah'; with 'لام' it occurs in all cases. When attributed to a servant, the first four words (mashi'ah etc.) become tamlik, and the last six (amr etc.) remain ta'liq. The passage also includes a commentary clarifying that the relied-upon position for such disputes is the Zahir al-Riwayah, as the Nawadir are not the madhhab. The discussion on 'ما شاء الله' and 'في علم الله' clarifies that non-occurrence depends on proper interpretation. This passage is a comprehensive guide to the nuances of istithna' in divorce and other acts.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/apparent transmission; the authoritative layer of transmission in the Hanafi school, comprising the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare transmissions; secondary sources that contain minority opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary in this lesson, when there is a difference of opinion in the Hanafi school, which transmission should the mufti follow?
A) The ruling found in the Nawadir.
B) The ruling found in al-Bazzaziyyah.
C) The apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah).
D) The ruling preferred by the later scholars.

Key Takeaway
In case of conflict, the mufti must rely on Zahir al-Riwayah, as it constitutes the madhhab.
